Refuting the Mu'tazila by Comparison to Magians
Al-Ash'ari refutes Mu'tazila by comparing them to Magians and citing a hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Ash'ari refutes the Mu'tazila by showing their doctrine parallels and exceeds the Magian belief in attributing power to other than Allah.

Core Idea
The Mu'tazila are worse than the Magians: both give others power Allah lacks.

Al-Ash'ari employs a powerful rhetorical argument by comparing the Mu'tazila to the Magians. The Magians claimed Satan can do evil that Allah cannot; the Mu'tazila claim disbelievers can do disbelief that Allah cannot. This passage reveals that the Mu'tazila not only share the Magian error but exceed it, and a prophetic hadith confirms the parallel.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the rhetorical question and the structure: first the Magian claim, then the Mu'tazila claim, then the hadith.
Pay attention to the word 'زدتم' (you have exceeded) – this is the key point.
2
Identify the two claims
Find the Magian claim about Satan and the Mu'tazila claim about disbelievers. How are they similar? How does the Mu'tazila claim 'exceed' the Magian claim?
The Magians limit Allah's power over evil; the Mu'tazila limit His power over disbelief, and they apply it to all disbelievers, not just a single being.
3
Understand the hadith proof
Read the hadith: 'The Qadariyya are the Magians of this Ummah.' Why does this prove the comparison? Because the Qadariyya (deniers of predestination) share the Magian belief in a power independent of Allah.
Al-Ash'ari uses the hadith to show that this is not merely a logical argument but rooted in revelation.
4
Reflect on the lesson
Ask yourself: What does this argument teach about divine omnipotence? How does it guard against compromising Allah's power?
This lesson reinforces the Sunni position that Allah is the sole creator and controller of all actions, good and evil.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الرد على المعتزلة : قال الشيخ أبو الحسن الأشعري رحمة الله عليه: ويقال لهم : أليس المجوس أثبتوا أن الشيطان يقدر على الشر الذي لا يقدر الله عز وجل عليه فكانوا بقولهم هذا كافرين ؟ فلا بد من نعم . فيقال لهم : فإذا زعمتم أن الكافرين يقدرون على الكفر، والله عز وجل لا يقدر عليه، فقد زدتم على المجوس في قولكم ؛ لأنكم تقولون معهم : إن الشيطان يقدر على الشر والله لا يقدر عليه وهذا مما يبينه الخبر عن رسول الله : (إِنَّ القَدَرِيَةَ مَجُوسُ هَذه الأمة ) ، وإنما صاروا مجوس هذه الأمة لأنهم قالوا بقول المجوس .
Refutation of the Mu'tazila: Sheikh Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, may Allah have mercy on him, said: And it is said to them: Did not the Magians affirm that Satan is able to do evil which Allah Almighty is not able to do, and thus they became disbelievers by this statement of theirs? So they must say 'yes'. Then it is said to them: So when you claim that the disbelievers are able to disbelief, and Allah Almighty is not able to it, then you have exceeded the Magians in your statement, because you say along with them: that Satan is able to evil and Allah is not able to it. And this is clarified by the report from the Messenger of Allah: 'Indeed the Qadariyya are the Magians of this Ummah', and they only became the Magians of this Ummah because they said the statement of the Magians.
Source pages p. 140

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Mu'tazila by exposing a parallel between their doctrine and that of the Magians. The Magians claimed that Satan can do evil that God cannot. Similarly, the Mu'tazila claim that disbelievers can perform disbelief that God cannot. The Ash'ari points out that if the Magians are disbelievers for this, then the Mu'tazila are even worse because they add the assignment of power to humans alongside Satan. The proof from the hadith identifies the Qadariyya (those who deny predestination) as the Magians of this Ummah, confirming the comparison.

Key Terms
المجوس
الشيطان
القدرية
الكفر
الشر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the Mu'tazila are only slightly mistaken about free will, but not as bad as polytheists.
Correction: Al-Ash'ari shows they exceed the Magians in disbelief because they give humans a power that rivals Allah's, similar to how Magians give Satan power over evil.

Checkpoint
Why does al-Ash'ari say the Mu'tazila exceed the Magians?
A) Because the Mu'tazila deny God's power over good.
B) Because the Mu'tazila claim that disbelievers can do what God cannot, just as Magians claim about Satan, and they say it about humans as well.
C) Because the Mu'tazila affirm God's power over evil.
D) Because the Mu'tazila are not monotheists.

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazila exceed the Magians in disbelief by claiming that disbelievers can do what Allah cannot, thereby compromising Allah's absolute power.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you sin, do you act as if you did it entirely by your own power, forgetting that Allah is the Creator of all actions? How does this lesson call you to repent from that hidden arrogance?
?
Have you ever doubted Allah's absolute power over all events, including evil, by saying 'Why did Allah allow this?' in a way that implies He was unable to stop it? What must you change in your heart after learning this?
?
If you truly believe that no one can do anything without Allah's will, how would your trust in Him reshape the way you face your greatest weakness today?

Definition of Qadari and Refutation of Opponents
Defines the term Qadari and argues the opponents are the true Qadariyya.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the polemical definition of 'Qadari' as used by Imam al-Ash'ari and how he turns the label back on his opponents.

Core Idea
The true Qadari claims to determine his own actions without Allah.

This passage from Imam al-Ash'ari's al-Ibanah presents a key theological argument about who deserves the label 'Qadari.' Rather than accepting the opponents' self-identification, al-Ash'ari redefines the term based on linguistic analogy and applies it to those who deny divine determination of actions. The passage is a masterclass in turning the tables through precise definition.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation once. Notice the structure: definition, linguistic analogy, application to opponents, and the author's own position.
2
Understand the definition
The author defines 'Qadari' as one who affirms predetermination (al-qadr) for himself, not for Allah.
This reverses the common usage of the term.
3
Analyze the linguistic analogy
The silversmith and carpenter examples show how language works: a craftsman is named by what he claims to do himself.
The analogy clarifies that the opponents are called Qadari because they claim to determine their own actions.
4
See the application
The opponents claim to determine their actions apart from Allah, so they are the Qadariyya. The author's group attributes all actions to Allah.
5
Reflect on the polemical move
This redefinition reverses the accusation, a common strategy in sectarian debates.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فيقال لهم : القدري هو من يثبت القدر لنفسه دون ربه عز وجل، وأنه يقدر أفعاله دون خالقه، وكذلك هو في اللغة؛ لأن الصائغ هو من زعم أنه يصوغ دون من يقول إنه يصاغ له، والنجار هو من يضيف النجارة إلى نفسه دون من يزعم أنه ينجر له، فلما كنتم تزعمون أنكم تقدرون أعمالكم وتفعلونها دون ربكم وجب أن تكونوا قدرية ولم نكن نحن قدرية ؛ لأنا لم نضف الأعمال إلى أنفسنا دون ربنا عز وجل، ولم نقل إنا نقدرها دونه، وقلنا: إنها تقدر لنا .
It is said to them: The Qadari is the one who affirms predetermination (al-qadr) for himself apart from his Lord, and that he determines his actions apart from his Creator. Similarly, it is in language: because the silversmith is the one who claims that he silvers without [attribution to] the one who says it is silvered for him, and the carpenter is the one who attributes carpentry to himself apart from the one who claims that it is carpentered for him. Since you claim that you determine (taqdirun) your actions and do them apart from your Lord, it is necessary that you be Qadariyya, and we are not Qadariyya, because we do not attribute actions to ourselves apart from our Lord, and we do not say that we determine them apart from Him; rather we say: they are determined (tuqaddaru) for us.
Source pages p. 141

Commentary
This passage is a definition and refutation. It begins by defining 'al-Qadari' as one who attributes predetermination (al-qadr) to himself rather than to Allah. The author then provides a linguistic analogy: just as a silversmith is called such because he claims to do the silversmithing without attributing it to another, so the opponent is called Qadari because he claims to determine his own actions without Allah. The author distinguishes his own position: they do not attribute actions to themselves but say actions are determined for them by Allah. Thus, the opponents are truly the Qadariyya, not the author's group.

Key Terms
قدري (Qadari)
القدر (al-qadr)
تقرير (taqdir)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The term Qadari refers to those who affirm divine predestination.
Correction: Imam al-Ash'ari defines Qadari as those who claim to determine their own actions without Allah, not those who affirm predestination.

Checkpoint
According to Imam Ashari, why are the opponents called 'Qadariyya'?
A) Because they affirm that Allah predestines all actions.
B) Because they claim to determine their own actions apart from Allah.
C) Because they deny predestination entirely.
D) Because they attribute carpentry to themselves.

Key Takeaway
The polemical label 'Qadari' is applied by Imam al-Ash'ari to those who claim to determine their own actions independently of Allah, using linguistic analogy to reverse the accusation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you succeed in a good deed, do you first thank Allah or quietly credit your own effort? Where does your heart go in that moment?
?
If you were to honestly trace every decision you made today back to its true source, would you find more of your own will or Allah's determination? What does that reveal about your reliance on Him?
?
You have just learned that the true Qadari is one who attributes actions to himself apart from Allah. Do you ever, even subtly, live as if your life is in your own hands? Will you today repent of that independence and declare that every action is determined for you?

Refuting the Qadari Accusation
Replies to the counter-argument that affirming Allah's predestination makes one Qadari.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Ash'ari uses a reductio ad absurdum to refute the claim that affirming divine predestination makes one a Qadari.

Core Idea
If affirming Allah's predestination made one a Qadari, the accusers would be Qadari themselves.

In this brief but powerful rejoinder, Imam al-Ash'ari turns the opponents' logic against them. He shows that their own definition—if applied consistently—would force them to accept the very label they reject. This passage is a masterclass in theological argumentation, using the opponent's own premises to undermine their position.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage carefully. Then read the literal translation to get the plain meaning. Pay attention to the logical structure: 'if...then...'.
2
Identify the opponent's claim
The opponent claims that affirming Allah's predestination (taqdir) makes one a Qadari. Note this as the premise being challenged.
This is the starting point of the rejoinder.
3
Follow the reductio ad absurdum
Al-Ash'ari shows that the opponent's own belief includes affirming Allah's predestination of the heavens, earth, and acts of obedience. Therefore, by their own logic, they would be Qadariyya. Since they reject this label, their initial claim is invalid.
This is the core logical move.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
The conclusion is that the opponent's argument is self-refuting. Affirming Allah's taqdir does not make one a Qadari; rather, it is a necessary belief. The earlier definition (that Qadari are those who claim predestination for themselves) stands.
The rejoinder is complete and forceful.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جواب : ويقال لهم : إذا كان من أثبت التقدير الله عز وجل قدرياً، فيلزمكم إذا زعمتم أن الله عز وجل قدر السموات والأرض وقدر الطاعات أن تكونوا قدرية، فإذا لم يلزم هذا فقد بطل قولكم وانتقض كلامكم
Answer: And it is said to them: If the one who affirms predetermination (al-taqdir) to Allah is a Qadari, then it follows that when you claim that Allah predetermined the heavens and the earth and predetermined acts of obedience, you become Qadariyya. If this does not follow, then your statement is invalidated and your speech is contradicted.
Source pages p. 141

Commentary
This passage is an answer (jawab) to a potential objection. The author employs a reductio ad absurdum: if affirming predetermination (al-taqdir) to Allah made one a Qadari, then the opponents themselves would be Qadari because they affirm that Allah predetermined the heavens, earth, and acts of obedience. Since they do not accept this label, their own criterion is self-refuting. Thus, the earlier definition stands: the Qadari is not one who affirms Allah's predetermination, but one who claims it for himself.

Key Terms
تقدير (taqdir)
قدرية (Qadariyya)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that affirming Allah's predestination is the defining feature of the Qadari sect.
Correction: This rejoinder shows that if that were the case, the opponents themselves would be Qadari for affirming Allah's predestination. The correct definition is that the Qadari is one who claims predestination for himself (i.e., denies divine decree).

Checkpoint
In the rejoinder, what consequence does Imam Ashari draw if the opponents' definition of Qadari were correct?
A) The opponents would be Qadariyya for affirming Allah's predestination.
B) The author's group would be Qadariyya for affirming Allah's predestination.
C) The definition would be proven correct.
D) The linguistic analogy would be invalid.

Key Takeaway
The rejoinder refutes the accusation by showing that if affirming divine predestination made one a Qadari, the accusers would be Qadari themselves, thus their argument is self-contradictory.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you are falsely accused of a wrong belief, do you immediately become defensive, or do you pause to examine whether the accusation actually applies to the accuser? This lesson teaches a precise logical move. How will you train yourself to respond with clarity rather than emotion the next time you face such a situation?
?
Do you truly believe that Allah's predestination includes all things—even your acts of obedience? If so, have you ever felt that this belief might be used against you by someone who misunderstands? How does this passage equip you to answer such objections with confidence and precision?
?
The opponent's argument collapsed because they held a double standard. Is there an area of your life where you judge others by a standard you do not apply to yourself? Let this passage's logic expose any inconsistency in your own heart, and commit to removing it today.

Allah's Foreknowledge: The Hadith of Adam and Musa
Imam Ash'ari cites the hadith of Adam and Musa to refute the Qadariyya claim of limited divine knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the hadith of Adam and Musa refutes the Qadariyya claim that Allah only knows events after they occur.

Core Idea
Allah's writing of destiny before creation proves His eternal knowledge.

Imam Ash'ari begins his refutation by citing a famous hadith in which Adam argues with Musa that his sin was written by Allah before the heavens were created. This hadith directly challenges the Qadariyya who assert that Allah does not know something until it happens. The author then draws the logical conclusion: if Allah wrote it, He must have known it.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith and the author's comment
Read the Arabic passage containing the hadith of Adam and Musa and the author's statement that it indicates the falsehood of the Qadariyya claim. Notice how the hadith is used as a proof.
2
Understand the Qadariyya claim
Identify the Qadariyya position: that Allah does not know the thing until it comes to be. Contrast this with the hadith's implication.
The Qadariyya were an early sect that denied predestination.
3
Analyze the logical inference
The author argues: if Allah wrote the deed and commanded it to be written, He cannot write something He does not know. Therefore, the hadith proves Allah's foreknowledge.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الَّذِي اصْطَفَاكَ الله بِكَلَامِهِ، تَلُومُنِي عَلَى عَمَلٍ كَتَبَهُ اللهُ عَلَيَّ قَبْلَ أَنْ يَخْلُقَ السَّمَاوَاتِ، قَالَ: فَحَجَّ آدَمُ مُوسَى. وَرُوِيَ حَدِيثُ حَجَّ آدَمُ مُوسَى مَالِكٌ عَنْ أَبِي الزِّنَادِ عَنِ الأَعْرَجِ عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ عَنِ النَّبِيِّ. وَهَذَا يَدُلُّ عَلَى بُطْلَانِ قَوْلِ الْقَدَرِيَّةِ الَّذِينَ يَقُولُونَ: إِنَّ اللهَ عَزَّ وَجَلَّ لَا يَعْلَمُ الشَّيْءَ حَتَّى يَكُونَ؛ لِأَنَّ اللهَ عَزَّ وَجَلَّ إِذَا كَتَبَ ذَلِكَ وَأَمَرَ بِأَنْ يُكْتَبَ فَلَا يَكْتُبُ شَيْئًا لَا يَعْلَمُهُ، جَلَّ عَنْ ذَلِكَ وَتَقَدَّسَ. وَقَالَ اللهُ عَزَّ وَجَلَّ: ﴿وَمَا نَسْقُطُ مِن وَرَقَةٍ إِلَّا يَعْلَمُهَا وَلَا حَبَّةٍ فِي ظُلُمَتِ الْأَرْضِ وَلَا رَطْبٍ وَلَا يَابِسٍ إِلَّا فِي كِتَبٍ مُّبِينٍ﴾ وَقَالَ: ﴿وَمَا مِن دَابَّةٍ فِي الْأَرْضِ إِلَّا عَلَى اللهِ رِزْقُهَا وَيَعْلَمُ مُسْتَقَرَّهَا وَمُسْتَوْدَعَهَا﴾ وَقَالَ: ﴿أَحْصَاهُ اللهُ وَنَسُوهُ﴾ وَقَالَ: ﴿لَقَدْ أَحْصَاهُمْ وَعَدَّهُمْ عَدًّا﴾ وَقَالَ: ﴿أَحَاطَ بِكُلِّ شَيْءٍ عِلْمًا وَأَحْصَى كُلَّ شَيْءٍ عَدَدًا﴾ وَقَالَ: ﴿بِكُلِّ شَيْءٍ عَلِيمٌ﴾ فَذَلِكَ يُبَيِّنُ أَنَّهُ يَعْلَمُ الْأَشْيَاءَ كُلَّهَا. وَقَدْ أَخْبَرَ اللهُ عَزَّ وَجَلَّ أَنَّ الْخَلْقَ يُبْعَثُونَ وَيُحْشَرُونَ، وَأَنَّ الْكَافِرِينَ فِي النَّارِ يُخَلَّدُونَ، وَأَنَّ الْأَنْبِيَاءَ وَالْمُؤْمِنِينَ فِي الْجِنَانِ يُخَلَّدُونَ، وَأَنَّ الْقِيَامَةَ تَقُومُ وَلَمْ تَقُمِ الْقِيَامَةُ بَعْدُ، فَذَلِكَ يَدُلُّ عَلَى أَنَّ اللهَ تَعَالَى يَعْلَمُ مَا يَكُونَ قَبْلَ أَنْ يَكُونَ. وَقَدْ قَالَ اللهُ فِي أَهْلِ النَّارِ: ﴿وَلَوْ رُدُّوا لَعَادُوا لِمَا نُهُوا عَنْهُ﴾ فَأَخْبَرَ عَمَّا لَا يَكُونُ أَنْ لَوْ كَانَ كَيْفَ يَكُونُ. وَقَالَ تَعَالَى: ﴿فَمَا بَالُ الْقُرُونِ الْأُولَى قَالَ عِلْمُهَا عِندَ رَبِّي فِي كِتَبٍ لَّا يَضِلُّ رَبِّي وَلَا يَنسَى﴾ وَمَنْ لَا يَعْلَمُ الشَّيْءَ قَبْلَ كَوْنِهِ لَا يَعْلَمُ بَعْدَ تَقَضِّيهِ، تَعَالَى اللهُ عَنْ قَوْلِ الظَّالِمِينَ عُلُوًّا كَبِيرًا.
He whom Allah chose with His speech, you blame me for a deed that Allah wrote upon me before He created the heavens. He said: So Adam argued with Musa. And the hadith of Adam arguing with Musa was narrated by Malik from Abu al-Zinad from al-A'raj from Abu Hurayrah from the Prophet. And this indicates the falsehood of the statement of the Qadariyya who say: Indeed Allah, Mighty and Majestic, does not know the thing until it comes to be; because Allah, Mighty and Majestic, if He wrote that and commanded that it be written, then He does not write something He does not know; He is exalted above that and sanctified. And Allah, Mighty and Majestic, said: {And no leaf falls but that He knows it, nor any grain in the darkness of the earth, nor anything wet or dry, but that it is in a clear Book} (6:59). And He said: {And there is no creature on earth but that upon Allah is its provision, and He knows its dwelling place and its repository} (11:6). And He said: {Allah has encompassed it and they forgot it} (58:6). And He said: {He has counted them and numbered them exactly} (19:94). And He said: {He encompasses everything in knowledge and has counted everything in number} (65:12, 72:28). And He said: {He is Knower of all things} (2:29). So that makes clear that He knows all things. And Allah, Mighty and Majestic, has informed that the creation will be raised and gathered, and that the disbelievers will abide eternally in the Fire, and that the prophets and believers will abide eternally in the Gardens, and that the Hour will come, though the Hour has not yet come. So that indicates that Allah, Exalted, knows what will be before it is. And Allah said concerning the people of the Fire: {If they were returned, they would return to what they were forbidden} (6:28); so He informed about what will not be, that if it were, how it would be. And He, Exalted, said: {What is the state of the former generations? He said: Their knowledge is with my Lord in a Book; my Lord does not err nor does He forget} (20:51-52). And whoever does not know the thing before its occurrence does not know after its passing. Exalted is Allah above the saying of the wrongdoers, greatly high.
Source pages p. 156

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Qadariyya sect who claim that Allah does not know events until they occur. The author begins by citing the hadith of Adam and Musa, in which Adam argues with Musa that the sin he committed was written by Allah before the creation of the heavens. The author then states that this hadith demonstrates the falsehood of the Qadariyya, because if Allah writes something and commands it to be written, He must know it; He is far above writing something unknown. Then the author quotes numerous Qur'anic verses to establish Allah's all-encompassing knowledge: the verse from Surah al-An'am that no leaf falls but He knows it; the verse from Surah Hud that every creature's provision and abode are known; the verse from Surah al-Mujadilah that Allah has encompassed them while they forgot; the verse from Surah Maryam that He has counted them exactly; the verse from Surah al-Talaq and al-Jinn that His knowledge surrounds everything and He has counted all things; and the verse from Surah al-Baqarah that He is Knower of all things. These verses show that Allah knows all things. Then the author argues from the fact that Allah has informed us that the creation will be resurrected, that the disbelievers will abide eternally in the Fire, and that the prophets and believers will abide eternally in Paradise, and that the Hour will come even though it has not yet come. This proves that Allah knows what will happen before it happens. Then the author cites the verse about the people of the Fire: 'If they were returned, they would return to what they were forbidden' (6:28) – Allah informed of what they would do if they were returned, which shows His knowledge of what would be. Then the verse from Surah Taha: 'What is the state of the former generations? He said: Their knowledge is with my Lord in a Book; my Lord does not err nor forget' (20:51-52). The author concludes that one who does not know a thing before it occurs cannot know it after it passes. The passage ends with a declaration of Allah's transcendence above the sayings of the wrongdoers.

Key Terms
القدرية
العلم
الكتاب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Qadariyya believed Allah only knows events after they happen.
Correction: The hadith shows Allah wrote the sin before creation, proving He knew it beforehand.

Checkpoint
How does the hadith of Adam and Musa refute the Qadariyya claim?
A) Adam argued that Musa had no right to blame him because the sin was written by Allah before creation, proving Allah knew it beforehand.
B) Musa argued that Adam had no excuse because the sin was not written.
C) The hadith shows that Adam and Musa disputed about predestination, but does not settle the issue.
D) The hadith proves that Allah does not know events until they happen.

Key Takeaway
The hadith of Adam and Musa proves that Allah's knowledge of events is prior to their occurrence because He wrote them before creation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Allah wrote every deed of yours before the heavens were created. Does this make you feel hopeless about changing your destiny, or does it fill you with awe at His perfect knowledge? How should this affect the way you approach repentance today?
?
When you sin, do you ever excuse yourself by thinking 'it was written'? How does Adam’s argument with Musa—that he still accepted responsibility despite the writing—challenge that excuse? What will you change in your next moment of weakness?
?
If Allah knows every secret thought you have not yet thought, what does that mean for the hidden parts of your life you prefer to ignore? Will you invite His knowledge to purify them, or continue to pretend they are unseen?

Qur'anic Verses on Allah's All-Encompassing Knowledge
Imam Ash'ari cites six Qur'anic verses to prove that Allah's knowledge is all-encompassing.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how multiple Qur'anic verses establish that Allah knows all things, including every leaf, grain, and creature.

Core Idea
Allah's knowledge encompasses all things, from the smallest leaf to the largest creation.

After the hadith, Imam Ash'ari marshals a series of Qur'anic verses that explicitly describe the extent of Allah's knowledge. These verses leave no room for the Qadariyya claim that Allah is ignorant of future events. Each verse emphasizes that nothing escapes His knowledge, and that all things are recorded in a clear Book.

Guided Path
1
Read the verses and the conclusion
Read the Arabic passage containing the six verses and the author's concluding statement. Notice the variety of examples: leaf, grain, creatures, counting, etc.
2
Identify the common theme
Each verse emphasizes that Allah knows all things. Look for keywords like 'knows', 'encompasses', 'counts'.
3
Understand the logical implication for the Qadariyya
If Allah knows every leaf and grain, He certainly knows future events. The author concludes that these verses show He knows all things.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الَّذِي اصْطَفَاكَ الله بِكَلَامِهِ، تَلُومُنِي عَلَى عَمَلٍ كَتَبَهُ اللهُ عَلَيَّ قَبْلَ أَنْ يَخْلُقَ السَّمَاوَاتِ، قَالَ: فَحَجَّ آدَمُ مُوسَى. وَرُوِيَ حَدِيثُ حَجَّ آدَمُ مُوسَى مَالِكٌ عَنْ أَبِي الزِّنَادِ عَنِ الأَعْرَجِ عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ عَنِ النَّبِيِّ. وَهَذَا يَدُلُّ عَلَى بُطْلَانِ قَوْلِ الْقَدَرِيَّةِ الَّذِينَ يَقُولُونَ: إِنَّ اللهَ عَزَّ وَجَلَّ لَا يَعْلَمُ الشَّيْءَ حَتَّى يَكُونَ؛ لِأَنَّ اللهَ عَزَّ وَجَلَّ إِذَا كَتَبَ ذَلِكَ وَأَمَرَ بِأَنْ يُكْتَبَ فَلَا يَكْتُبُ شَيْئًا لَا يَعْلَمُهُ، جَلَّ عَنْ ذَلِكَ وَتَقَدَّسَ. وَقَالَ اللهُ عَزَّ وَجَلَّ: ﴿وَمَا نَسْقُطُ مِن وَرَقَةٍ إِلَّا يَعْلَمُهَا وَلَا حَبَّةٍ فِي ظُلُمَتِ الْأَرْضِ وَلَا رَطْبٍ وَلَا يَابِسٍ إِلَّا فِي كِتَبٍ مُّبِينٍ﴾ وَقَالَ: ﴿وَمَا مِن دَابَّةٍ فِي الْأَرْضِ إِلَّا عَلَى اللهِ رِزْقُهَا وَيَعْلَمُ مُسْتَقَرَّهَا وَمُسْتَوْدَعَهَا﴾ وَقَالَ: ﴿أَحْصَاهُ اللهُ وَنَسُوهُ﴾ وَقَالَ: ﴿لَقَدْ أَحْصَاهُمْ وَعَدَّهُمْ عَدًّا﴾ وَقَالَ: ﴿أَحَاطَ بِكُلِّ شَيْءٍ عِلْمًا وَأَحْصَى كُلَّ شَيْءٍ عَدَدًا﴾ وَقَالَ: ﴿بِكُلِّ شَيْءٍ عَلِيمٌ﴾ فَذَلِكَ يُبَيِّنُ أَنَّهُ يَعْلَمُ الْأَشْيَاءَ كُلَّهَا. وَقَدْ أَخْبَرَ اللهُ عَزَّ وَجَلَّ أَنَّ الْخَلْقَ يُبْعَثُونَ وَيُحْشَرُونَ، وَأَنَّ الْكَافِرِينَ فِي النَّارِ يُخَلَّدُونَ، وَأَنَّ الْأَنْبِيَاءَ وَالْمُؤْمِنِينَ فِي الْجِنَانِ يُخَلَّدُونَ، وَأَنَّ الْقِيَامَةَ تَقُومُ وَلَمْ تَقُمِ الْقِيَامَةُ بَعْدُ، فَذَلِكَ يَدُلُّ عَلَى أَنَّ اللهَ تَعَالَى يَعْلَمُ مَا يَكُونَ قَبْلَ أَنْ يَكُونَ. وَقَدْ قَالَ اللهُ فِي أَهْلِ النَّارِ: ﴿وَلَوْ رُدُّوا لَعَادُوا لِمَا نُهُوا عَنْهُ﴾ فَأَخْبَرَ عَمَّا لَا يَكُونُ أَنْ لَوْ كَانَ كَيْفَ يَكُونُ. وَقَالَ تَعَالَى: ﴿فَمَا بَالُ الْقُرُونِ الْأُولَى قَالَ عِلْمُهَا عِندَ رَبِّي فِي كِتَبٍ لَّا يَضِلُّ رَبِّي وَلَا يَنسَى﴾ وَمَنْ لَا يَعْلَمُ الشَّيْءَ قَبْلَ كَوْنِهِ لَا يَعْلَمُ بَعْدَ تَقَضِّيهِ، تَعَالَى اللهُ عَنْ قَوْلِ الظَّالِمِينَ عُلُوًّا كَبِيرًا.
He whom Allah chose with His speech, you blame me for a deed that Allah wrote upon me before He created the heavens. He said: So Adam argued with Musa. And the hadith of Adam arguing with Musa was narrated by Malik from Abu al-Zinad from al-A'raj from Abu Hurayrah from the Prophet. And this indicates the falsehood of the statement of the Qadariyya who say: Indeed Allah, Mighty and Majestic, does not know the thing until it comes to be; because Allah, Mighty and Majestic, if He wrote that and commanded that it be written, then He does not write something He does not know; He is exalted above that and sanctified. And Allah, Mighty and Majestic, said: {And no leaf falls but that He knows it, nor any grain in the darkness of the earth, nor anything wet or dry, but that it is in a clear Book} (6:59). And He said: {And there is no creature on earth but that upon Allah is its provision, and He knows its dwelling place and its repository} (11:6). And He said: {Allah has encompassed it and they forgot it} (58:6). And He said: {He has counted them and numbered them exactly} (19:94). And He said: {He encompasses everything in knowledge and has counted everything in number} (65:12, 72:28). And He said: {He is Knower of all things} (2:29). So that makes clear that He knows all things. And Allah, Mighty and Majestic, has informed that the creation will be raised and gathered, and that the disbelievers will abide eternally in the Fire, and that the prophets and believers will abide eternally in the Gardens, and that the Hour will come, though the Hour has not yet come. So that indicates that Allah, Exalted, knows what will be before it is. And Allah said concerning the people of the Fire: {If they were returned, they would return to what they were forbidden} (6:28); so He informed about what will not be, that if it were, how it would be. And He, Exalted, said: {What is the state of the former generations? He said: Their knowledge is with my Lord in a Book; my Lord does not err nor does He forget} (20:51-52). And whoever does not know the thing before its occurrence does not know after its passing. Exalted is Allah above the saying of the wrongdoers, greatly high.
Source pages p. 156

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Qadariyya sect who claim that Allah does not know events until they occur. The author begins by citing the hadith of Adam and Musa, in which Adam argues with Musa that the sin he committed was written by Allah before the creation of the heavens. The author then states that this hadith demonstrates the falsehood of the Qadariyya, because if Allah writes something and commands it to be written, He must know it; He is far above writing something unknown. Then the author quotes numerous Qur'anic verses to establish Allah's all-encompassing knowledge: the verse from Surah al-An'am that no leaf falls but He knows it; the verse from Surah Hud that every creature's provision and abode are known; the verse from Surah al-Mujadilah that Allah has encompassed them while they forgot; the verse from Surah Maryam that He has counted them exactly; the verse from Surah al-Talaq and al-Jinn that His knowledge surrounds everything and He has counted all things; and the verse from Surah al-Baqarah that He is Knower of all things. These verses show that Allah knows all things. Then the author argues from the fact that Allah has informed us that the creation will be resurrected, that the disbelievers will abide eternally in the Fire, and that the prophets and believers will abide eternally in Paradise, and that the Hour will come even though it has not yet come. This proves that Allah knows what will happen before it happens. Then the author cites the verse about the people of the Fire: 'If they were returned, they would return to what they were forbidden' (6:28) – Allah informed of what they would do if they were returned, which shows His knowledge of what would be. Then the verse from Surah Taha: 'What is the state of the former generations? He said: Their knowledge is with my Lord in a Book; my Lord does not err nor forget' (20:51-52). The author concludes that one who does not know a thing before it occurs cannot know it after it passes. The passage ends with a declaration of Allah's transcendence above the sayings of the wrongdoers.

الكتاب
الإحصاء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following verses is NOT cited in this passage?
A) And no leaf falls but that He knows it
B) And there is no creature on earth but that upon Allah is its provision
C) He knows what is in the heavens and the earth
D) He encompasses everything in knowledge

Key Takeaway
The Qur'anic verses explicitly state that Allah's knowledge covers every detail of creation, refuting the idea that He is unaware of future events.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you sin in secret, do you truly believe that Allah sees every leaf fall and every grain, and that He knows your hidden action? How would your behavior change if you lived with that certainty every moment?
?
Allah has counted every detail of your life—your breaths, your thoughts, your intentions. Does this comfort you or frighten you? Will you let it lead you to gratitude and repentance, or to heedlessness?
?
If Allah knows the future of every leaf, then He knows your tomorrow, your next year, and your final breath. Are you living as if you believe that, or are you planning your life as if you control it? What needs to change today?

Eschatological Proofs and Hypothetical Knowledge
Imam Ash'ari uses eschatological predictions and hypothetical knowledge to further prove Allah's foreknowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Allah's predictions of future events and His knowledge of hypotheticals prove His foreknowledge.

Core Idea
Allah's accurate predictions of the resurrection and the afterlife prove He knows all future events.

Imam Ash'ari continues his refutation by pointing to Allah's explicit statements about events that have not yet occurred: the resurrection, the eternal fate of disbelievers and believers, and even hypothetical scenarios like 'if they were returned'. Such statements would be impossible if Allah only knew things after they happen. This lesson explores these arguments.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on eschatological predictions
Read the Arabic passage where the author mentions that Allah has informed of the resurrection, the eternal abodes, and the Hour that has not yet come.
2
Understand the argument
If Allah tells us about events that will certainly happen in the future, He must know them beforehand. Otherwise, He could not inform about them.
3
Examine the hypothetical verse
The verse about the people of the Fire being returned shows Allah knows what would happen even in a counterfactual situation. This proves His knowledge extends to all possibilities.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
The author concludes that one who does not know before an event cannot know after it passes, and declares Allah transcendent above such limitations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الَّذِي اصْطَفَاكَ الله بِكَلَامِهِ، تَلُومُنِي عَلَى عَمَلٍ كَتَبَهُ اللهُ عَلَيَّ قَبْلَ أَنْ يَخْلُقَ السَّمَاوَاتِ، قَالَ: فَحَجَّ آدَمُ مُوسَى. وَرُوِيَ حَدِيثُ حَجَّ آدَمُ مُوسَى مَالِكٌ عَنْ أَبِي الزِّنَادِ عَنِ الأَعْرَجِ عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ عَنِ النَّبِيِّ. وَهَذَا يَدُلُّ عَلَى بُطْلَانِ قَوْلِ الْقَدَرِيَّةِ الَّذِينَ يَقُولُونَ: إِنَّ اللهَ عَزَّ وَجَلَّ لَا يَعْلَمُ الشَّيْءَ حَتَّى يَكُونَ؛ لِأَنَّ اللهَ عَزَّ وَجَلَّ إِذَا كَتَبَ ذَلِكَ وَأَمَرَ بِأَنْ يُكْتَبَ فَلَا يَكْتُبُ شَيْئًا لَا يَعْلَمُهُ، جَلَّ عَنْ ذَلِكَ وَتَقَدَّسَ. وَقَالَ اللهُ عَزَّ وَجَلَّ: ﴿وَمَا نَسْقُطُ مِن وَرَقَةٍ إِلَّا يَعْلَمُهَا وَلَا حَبَّةٍ فِي ظُلُمَتِ الْأَرْضِ وَلَا رَطْبٍ وَلَا يَابِسٍ إِلَّا فِي كِتَبٍ مُّبِينٍ﴾ وَقَالَ: ﴿وَمَا مِن دَابَّةٍ فِي الْأَرْضِ إِلَّا عَلَى اللهِ رِزْقُهَا وَيَعْلَمُ مُسْتَقَرَّهَا وَمُسْتَوْدَعَهَا﴾ وَقَالَ: ﴿أَحْصَاهُ اللهُ وَنَسُوهُ﴾ وَقَالَ: ﴿لَقَدْ أَحْصَاهُمْ وَعَدَّهُمْ عَدًّا﴾ وَقَالَ: ﴿أَحَاطَ بِكُلِّ شَيْءٍ عِلْمًا وَأَحْصَى كُلَّ شَيْءٍ عَدَدًا﴾ وَقَالَ: ﴿بِكُلِّ شَيْءٍ عَلِيمٌ﴾ فَذَلِكَ يُبَيِّنُ أَنَّهُ يَعْلَمُ الْأَشْيَاءَ كُلَّهَا. وَقَدْ أَخْبَرَ اللهُ عَزَّ وَجَلَّ أَنَّ الْخَلْقَ يُبْعَثُونَ وَيُحْشَرُونَ، وَأَنَّ الْكَافِرِينَ فِي النَّارِ يُخَلَّدُونَ، وَأَنَّ الْأَنْبِيَاءَ وَالْمُؤْمِنِينَ فِي الْجِنَانِ يُخَلَّدُونَ، وَأَنَّ الْقِيَامَةَ تَقُومُ وَلَمْ تَقُمِ الْقِيَامَةُ بَعْدُ، فَذَلِكَ يَدُلُّ عَلَى أَنَّ اللهَ تَعَالَى يَعْلَمُ مَا يَكُونَ قَبْلَ أَنْ يَكُونَ. وَقَدْ قَالَ اللهُ فِي أَهْلِ النَّارِ: ﴿وَلَوْ رُدُّوا لَعَادُوا لِمَا نُهُوا عَنْهُ﴾ فَأَخْبَرَ عَمَّا لَا يَكُونُ أَنْ لَوْ كَانَ كَيْفَ يَكُونُ. وَقَالَ تَعَالَى: ﴿فَمَا بَالُ الْقُرُونِ الْأُولَى قَالَ عِلْمُهَا عِندَ رَبِّي فِي كِتَبٍ لَّا يَضِلُّ رَبِّي وَلَا يَنسَى﴾ وَمَنْ لَا يَعْلَمُ الشَّيْءَ قَبْلَ كَوْنِهِ لَا يَعْلَمُ بَعْدَ تَقَضِّيهِ، تَعَالَى اللهُ عَنْ قَوْلِ الظَّالِمِينَ عُلُوًّا كَبِيرًا.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think Allah's knowledge is limited to the present.

Checkpoint
What does the verse about the people of the Fire (وَلَوْ رُدُّوا لَعَادُوا) demonstrate about Allah's knowledge?
A) Allah knows only actual events.
B) Allah knows what would have happened even in counterfactual scenarios.
C) Allah does not know the future.
D) The verse is metaphorical and not about knowledge.

Allah's accurate reports of future events and hypotheticals prove that His knowledge precedes all events, both actual and possible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Allah has informed you of the resurrection and your eternal destination based on your faith. If you were to die tonight, would you be among those who 'abide eternally in the Gardens' or 'in the Fire'? What is one thing you can do today to change the answer?
?
Allah knows even the hypothetical: what you would do if you were given a second chance. Consider a sin you have committed. If you were returned to that moment, would you truly avoid it? Be honest. What does that say about your heart's inclination?
?
The verse says 'my Lord does not err nor does He forget.' You, however, forget His commands and err in your obedience. How can you keep the reality of the Hour and the Hereafter so present in your mind that you never forget your purpose?

The Decisiveness of Outward Consensus: Ash'ari's Proof for Abu Bakr's Caliphate
Ash'ari argues that outward consensus on Abu Bakr's caliphate is decisive.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ash'ari uses the outward consensus of the Companions, including Ali and Abbas, as a definitive proof for Abu Bakr's imamate, and why he rejects appeals to hidden intentions.

Core Idea
Outward consensus is binding; hidden intentions cannot undermine what is publicly established.

Ash'ari presents a key proof for Abu Bakr's caliphate based on the fact that all Muslims, including those later claimed to be opponents, gave him allegiance outwardly. He then counters a potential objection that their inward state might have been different, arguing that Islamic law only judges by outward actions. This lesson examines that argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation. Notice the structure: a proof, an objection, and a rebuttal.
The passage is dense; let it sink in before moving to analysis.
2
Identify the three positions on imamate
The passage lists three sectarian claims about who was explicitly designated for the caliphate: Abu Bakr, Ali, or al-Abbas. Note how Ash'ari frames these as the only possible positions.
The Rafidah and Rawandiyyah are the ones advocating for Ali and al-Abbas respectively.
3
Analyze the core argument from consensus
Ash'ari argues that the outward allegiance of Ali and al-Abbas to Abu Bakr, along with all Muslims, establishes consensus. See how he uses their public actions as evidence.
Even those who claimed a different explicit designation outwardly accepted Abu Bakr.
4
Understand the rebuttal against hidden intentions
Ash'ari anticipates an objection: perhaps Ali and al-Abbas inwardly opposed Abu Bakr. He rejects this because Islamic law only judges by outward appearances (zahir), not inner states (batin).
If hidden intentions could invalidate consensus, no consensus would ever be valid.
5
Reflect on the conclusion
The passage concludes that consensus on Abu Bakr's imamate is firmly established by outward actions. Consider why this principle is important in Islamic legal theory.
This argument protects the validity of historical consensus from subjective skepticism.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
دليل آخر للإجماع على إمامة أبي بكر رضي الله عنه : ومما يدل على إمامة الصديق أن المسلمين جميعاً بايعوه وانقادوا لإمامته، وقالوا له: يا خليفة رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ، ورأينا علياً والعباس رضي الله عنهما بايعاه ، وأقرا له بالإمامة . وإذا كانت الرافضة يقولون : إن عليا لله هو المنصوص على إمامته، والراوندية تقول : العباس هو المنصوص على إمامته . ولم يكن للناس في الإمامة إلا ثلاثة أقوال : من قال منهم : إن النبيل نص على إمامة الصديق ، وهو الإمام بعد الرسول صلى الله عليه وسلم ، وقول من قال: نص على إمامة عليه، وقول من قال: الإمام بعده العباس رضي الله عنه وقول من قال: هو أبو بكر الصديق الله هو بإجماع المسلمين والشهادة له بذلك ، ثم رأينا علياً والعباس رضي الله عنهما قد بايعـاه وأجمعـا علـى إمامته، فوجب أن يكون إماماً بعد النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم بإجماع المسلمين . ولا يجوز لقائل أن يقول : كان باطن علي والعباس رضي الله عنهما خلاف ظاهرهما، ولو جاز هذا لمدعيه لم يصح إجماع، وجاز لقائل أن يقول ذلك في كل إجماع للمسلمين، وهذا يسقط حجة الإجماع؛ لأن الله عز وجل لم يتعبدنا في الإجماع بباطن الناس، وإنما تعبدنا بظاهرهم، وإذا كان كذلك فقد حصل الإجماع والاتفاق على إمامة أبي بكر الصديق
Another proof for the consensus on the imamate of Abu Bakr, may Allah be pleased with him: Among the evidence for the imamate of al-Siddiq is that all the Muslims gave him allegiance and submitted to his imamate, and they said to him: O Caliph of the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, and we saw Ali and al-Abbas, may Allah be pleased with them, giving him allegiance and acknowledging his imamate. And if the Rafidah say that Ali, may Allah be pleased with him, is the one explicitly designated for his imamate, and the Rawandiyyah say that al-Abbas is the one explicitly designated for his imamate. And there were among the people only three statements concerning the imamate: The statement of those who say that the Prophet explicitly designated al-Siddiq for the imamate, and he is the caliph after the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace; and the statement of those who say that he explicitly designated Ali; and the statement of those who say that the caliph after him is al-Abbas, may Allah be pleased with him; and the statement of those who say: He is Abu Bakr al-Siddiq, may Allah be pleased with him, by the consensus of the Muslims and the testimony to that effect. Then we saw that Ali and al-Abbas, may Allah be pleased with them, gave him allegiance and agreed upon his imamate. So it is obligatory that he be the caliph after the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, by the consensus of the Muslims. And it is not permissible for anyone to say that the inner state of Ali and al-Abbas was contrary to their outward appearance. If this were permissible for its claimant, no consensus would be valid, and it would be permissible for anyone to say that in every consensus of the Muslims, and this would invalidate the proof of consensus; because Allah, the Mighty and Majestic, did not obligate us in matters of consensus to know the inner states of people, but rather He obligated us to follow their outward appearances. And if this is the case, then the consensus and agreement on the imamate of Abu Bakr al-Siddiq has been established.
Source pages p. 170

Commentary
This passage presents a proof for the legitimacy of Abu Bakr's caliphate based on consensus (ijma'). The author begins by stating the fact that all Muslims, including Ali and al-Abbas, outwardly pledged allegiance and called him 'Caliph of the Messenger of Allah.' Then he notes the objections of two sects: the Rafidah claim that Ali was explicitly designated, and the Rawandiyyah claim the same for al-Abbas. He reduces the possible positions to three: that the Prophet explicitly nominated Abu Bakr, or Ali, or al-Abbas. He then reaffirms that Ali and al-Abbas themselves agreed to Abu Bakr's imamate publicly. The core argument is that consensus is established by outward actions, not hidden intentions. If someone claims that Ali and al-Abbas inwardly opposed Abu Bakr despite their outward allegiance, they would destroy the entire principle of consensus, because Sharia only holds us to outward appearances. Therefore, the outward consensus is sufficient to prove Abu Bakr's imamate.

Key Terms
الإجماع (ijma')
الرافضة (Rafidah)
الراوندية (Rawandiyyah)
باطن (batin/inner)
ظاهر (zahir/outer)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The inner opposition of some Companions could invalidate the consensus on Abu Bakr's caliphate.
Correction: Islamic law does not require us to know inner states; consensus is established by outward actions alone.

Checkpoint
Why does the author reject the claim that Ali and al-Abbas inwardly opposed Abu Bakr despite their outward allegiance?
A) Because such a claim cannot be proven historically.
B) Because Allah does not obligate us to know inner states; we judge by outward actions.
C) Because Ali and al-Abbas explicitly stated their approval in writing.
D) Because the Prophet forbade questioning the sincerity of companions.

Key Takeaway
Outward consensus of the Companions, especially the allegiance of Ali and Abbas, proves the legitimacy of Abu Bakr's caliphate, and any claim of hidden dissent is irrelevant because Sharia only considers outward actions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When have I refused to accept someone's outward good actions because I assumed their inner intentions were wrong? How can I change that?
?
If Allah judges by our outward obedience in matters of community consensus, do I prioritize my private opinions over the collective agreement of the believers?
?
Am I willing to submit to legitimate leadership even if I have inner reservations, knowing that Sharia holds me to my outward allegiance?

Proof of Umar's Imamate through Abu Bakr's Appointment
Ash'ari states that Umar's caliphate follows from Abu Bakr's designation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Ash'ari proves the legitimacy of Umar's caliphate by linking it to the established imamate of Abu Bakr.

Core Idea
Umar's caliphate is validated through Abu Bakr's legitimate appointment.

Imam al-Ash'ari presents a concise logical proof: once the imamate of Abu Bakr (al-Siddiq) is established, the imamate of Umar (al-Faruq) follows directly. This relies on the historical fact that Abu Bakr designated Umar as his successor. In this lesson, we examine this reasoning and its significance in defending Sunni positions on the caliphate.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Begin by reading the original Arabic line and its English translation to understand the direct claim. Notice the conditional structure.
The passage is very short; this is the complete argument.
2
Understand the logical structure
The passage uses an 'if...then' conditional to link Umar's imamate to Abu Bakr's. Recognize that this is a chain of authority: Abu Bakr's imamate is already proven, and his appointment of Umar is accepted as valid.
3
Consider the underlying assumptions
The argument assumes the historical fact of Abu Bakr's appointment of Umar and the legitimacy of Abu Bakr's own caliphate. The passage expects the reader to accept these premises.
This argument is part of a larger discussion on the legitimacy of the caliphs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا ثبتت إمامة الصديق ثبتت إمامة الفاروق
And if the imamate of al-Siddiq is established, then the imamate of al-Faruq is established.
Source pages p. 170

Commentary
This short passage is a logical conclusion: once Abu Bakr's (al-Siddiq) caliphate is proven, then Umar's (al-Faruq) caliphate is also proven because Abu Bakr appointed him. The author presumes the reader knows that Abu Bakr designated Umar as his successor (the historical fact is assumed). This is a simple proof by chain of transmission of authority.

Key Terms
الصديق (al-Siddiq)
الفاروق (al-Faruq)
إمامة (imamate)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That Umar's caliphate was established through consensus or election independent of Abu Bakr.
Correction: Imam al-Ash'ari asserts that Umar's imamate is established specifically because Abu Bakr's imamate is established and Abu Bakr appointed him.

Checkpoint

A) By direct divine revelation.
B) By the consensus of the Muslims after Abu Bakr's death.
C) By the fact that Abu Bakr's imamate is established and he appointed Umar.
D) By Umar's own superior qualifications.

Key Takeaway
The legitimacy of Umar's caliphate is derived from the established imamate of Abu Bakr and his appointment.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This lesson shows that Umar's authority rests on Abu Bakr's. Do you sincerely accept both caliphates without reservation? What would need to change in your heart to fully submit to this chain of authority?
?
If you were to defend the legitimacy of the early caliphate to someone who doubts, how would your understanding of this conditional proof shape your argument? Are you prepared to stand by this reasoning?

Proof for Uthman's Imamate by the Shura Council
Ash'ari affirms Uthman's caliphate by shura council.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Uthman's caliphate was established through a legitimate shura process initiated by Umar, ensuring consensus among the appointed council.

Core Idea
Uthman's imamate was validated by the shura council's unanimous choice.

In this passage, Imam Ash'ari argues for the legitimacy of Uthman's caliphate by referencing the shura council appointed by Umar. The council members, all respected companions, unanimously chose Uthman and agreed on his merit. This demonstrates that Uthman's succession was based on a contractual process rather than mere appointment or force.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text carefully. Note the key terms: ثبوت (establishment), عقد (contract), الشورى (shura).
The passage is concise but packed with meaning.
2
Identify the key players
Umar appointed the shura council; Uthman was chosen by them. Understand that the council's consensus gives legitimacy.
3
Reflect on the significance
Why is this important? It counters claims that Uthman's caliphate was controversial. The author emphasizes agreement on his virtue and justice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وثبتت إمامة عثمان له بعد عمره بعقد من عقد له الإمامة من أصحاب الشورى الذين نص عليهم عمر فاختاروه ورضوا بإمامته، وأجمعوا على فضله وعدله
And the imamate of Uthman is established for him after Umar by the contract of those who contracted the imamate for him from among the people of the shura whom Umar designated, so they chose him and were pleased with his imamate, and they agreed upon his merit and justice.
Source pages p. 170

Commentary
This passage establishes Uthman's caliphate by the method of shura (consultative council). Umar, before his death, appointed a council of six companions to choose the next caliph. They chose Uthman, and all agreed on his excellence and justice. Thus, his imamate is valid by the consensus of the shura members, which in turn was authorized by the previous caliph Umar.

Misconception & Correction

Correction: Ash'ari shows that Uthman was chosen by a shura council appointed by Umar, with full consensus, establishing a valid contractual basis.

Checkpoint

A) By direct nomination from the Prophet.
B) By the shura council designated by Umar.
C) By popular acclamation after Umar's death.
D) By hereditary succession from Abu Bakr.

Key Takeaway
Uthman's caliphate was legitimized by the consensus of the shura council appointed by Umar.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

When you think about the leaders over you in your community or family, are you genuinely pleased with them, or do you harbor discontent that undermines unity? What concrete step can you take today to adopt the attitude of the companions?
?
Uthman's imamate was established by a contract of consultation. Have you taken seriously your own bay'ah to obey legitimate authority, even when it doesn't align with your personal desires? Will you renew that commitment today, seeking Allah's pleasure through obedience to those in charge?

The Legitimacy of Umar and Uthman's Caliphates
Statements on the legitimacy of the caliphates of Umar and Uthman

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Sunni doctrine affirms the legitimacy of the caliphates of Umar and Uthman through explicit designation and consensus of the shura council.

Core Idea
Umar was appointed by Abu Bakr; Uthman by the shura council's contract.

This passage from Imam al-Ash'ari's al-Ibanah provides a succinct affirmation of the rightful caliphates of Umar and Uthman. It grounds Umar's succession in Abu Bakr's explicit designation and Uthman's in the consensus of the shura council appointed by Umar. Understanding these foundations is key to Sunni political theology.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to grasp the two separate claims about Umar and Uthman.
Notice the structure: first Umar, then Uthman.
2
Identify the basis for Umar's caliphate
The passage states that Abu Bakr explicitly designated Umar and contracted the imamate for him. Consider why this is significant for Sunni legitimacy.
3
Identify the basis for Uthman's caliphate
Uthman's imamate was established by the contract of the people of the shura, whom Umar had designated. They chose Uthman and agreed on his virtue and justice.
4
Reflect on the doctrine
Ask yourself: How does this passage defend Sunni views against challenges? What does it imply about the legitimacy of the early caliphs?
This connects to the sectarian discussions of the time.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لأن الصديق رضي الله عنه نص عليه وعقد له الإمامة، واختاره لها، وكان أفضلهم بعد أبي بكر رضي الله عنهما . ٢٦٩ - وثبتت إمامة عثمان (۱) له بعد عمره بعقد من عقد له الإمامة من أصحاب الشورى الذين نص عليهم عمر فاختاروه ورضوا بإمامته، وأجمعوا على فضله وعدله
Because al-Siddiq (Abu Bakr), may Allah be pleased with him, designated him (Umar) and contracted the imamate for him, and chose him for it, and he was the best of them after Abu Bakr, may Allah be pleased with them both. (269) And the imamate of Uthman was established after Umar by the contract of those who contracted the imamate for him from the people of the shura whom Umar had designated, so they chose him and were pleased with his imamate, and they agreed on his virtue and justice.
Source pages p. 171

Commentary
This passage presents two concise statements affirming the legitimacy of the caliphates of Umar and Uthman. First, it states that Abu Bakr explicitly designated Umar and contracted the imamate for him, indicating that Umar was chosen by the best of the Companions after Abu Bakr himself. Second, it asserts that Uthman's imamate was established by the contract (ʿaqd) of the people of the shura (ahl al-shūrā), the council appointed by Umar. These individuals chose Uthman, expressed satisfaction with his leadership, and agreed on his virtue and justice. This demonstrates the Sunni doctrine that the caliphate of the first three caliphs was legitimate: Abu Bakr by direct appointment, Umar by Abu Bakr's designation, and Uthman by the consensus of the shura council.

Key Terms
الصديق
الإمامة
أصحاب الشورى
عقد
إجماع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think Uthman's caliphate was not based on consensus.
Correction: The passage affirms that Uthman's imamate was established by the contract of the shura council, who agreed on his virtue and justice.

Checkpoint
How was Uthman's imamate established according to this passage?
A) By direct appointment of Umar
B) By contract from the people of the shura
C) By popular election
D) By military force

Key Takeaway
The passage affirms that Umar's caliphate was by Abu Bakr's designation and Uthman's by the consensus of the shura council, establishing the Sunni position on their legitimacy.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Companions of the shura council were completely satisfied with Uthman's imamate and agreed on his virtue. When you look at the leaders in your own life—in your family, mosque, or community—can you honestly say you are pleased with their leadership? What would it take for you to reach that level of contentment and public affirmation? Will you actively seek to see the good in those above you, even if you don't agree with every decision?
?
The passage highlights that legitimacy came through a clear process: designation by the previous leader (Abu Bakr for Umar) and consultation and contract (shura for Uthman). Are you a person who respects and submits to legitimate authority, or do you tend to question and resist it in your heart? Reflect on a specific leader you find hard to accept. What would it mean for you to recognize God's wisdom in the way they came to power?
?
Umar was described as 'the best after Abu Bakr'. In your interactions, do you evaluate people by their virtue and justice, or by superficial qualities like charisma or popularity? Imagine you were part of the shura council. What criteria would you use to choose a leader? Commit today to prioritizing character over convenience in your own judgments of leadership.

The Emergence of Abdullah ibn Saba and the Secret Propaganda
Background of Uthman's popularity and emergence of Ibn Saba's secret campaign.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how a single individual, Abdullah ibn Saba, initiated the fitna against Uthman through secret propaganda.

Core Idea
One man's secret propaganda ignited the fitna that fractured the Muslim community.

This lesson examines the early origins of the fitna (civil strife) during Uthman's caliphate. The author, Muhammad al-Khidr Husayn, identifies a key figure, Abdullah ibn Saba, whose insincere conversion and covert activities laid the groundwork for opposition. We will read how he moved from city to city, gathering followers and spreading his message.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing it. Then read the translation. Notice the contrast between Uthman's initial popularity and the emergence of insincere converts.
The passage begins by describing Uthman's popularity and then introduces Ibn Saba.
2
Identify the key figure
Focus on Abdullah ibn Saba's background and actions. Note his Jewish origin, his secret propaganda, and his travels to different cities.
He is described as 'from the Jews of Himyar' and settles in various places.
3
Trace the spread of propaganda
Observe how Ibn Saba's message spreads from secret circles to preachers sent to other cities. Reflect on the author's emphasis on this organized campaign.
He sends preachers to the lands from which he was expelled.

قال الإمام الأكبر محمد الخضر حسين شيخ الأزهر تحت عنوان : كيف نشأت الفتنة؟ قضى عثمان معظم أيام خلافته والناس مجمعون على حبه والاغتباط بإمارته لشدة رأفته وواسع حلمه ولين جانبه، ولأن أيدي الناس امتلأت في عهده من المغانم، وصاروا يتمتعون بالعيش الطيب أكثر مما كانوا يتمتعون . كان بعد هذا أن دخل في الإسلام نفر غير مخلصين في إسلامهم، وإنما يريدون الكيد له، وتفريق كلمة أهله من هؤلاء عبد الله بن سبأ المعروف بابن السوداء. وهو من يهود حمير، نزل البصرة على حكيم بن جبلة العبدي، وابتدأ يبث في السر أن علياً أحق في الخلافة، ويدعو إلى نزع الخلافة من عثمان، فتعلق بدعوته نفر، وبلغ أمره عبد الله بن عامر البصرة، فطرده، وجاء الكوفة فأخرج منها ، ثم جاء الشام فأخرج منها كذلك، فأتى مصر واتصل به نفر من أوشاب كنانة الناس، منهم بن بشر وخالد بن ملجم، وأخذ يردد عليهم أن علياً وصي النبي ، وأن عثمان أخذ الخلافة بغير حق، وبعث من هؤلاء دعاة في البلاد التي كان قد طرد منها، واتفق أن كان لعثمان عمال من ذوي ،قرابته، وهناك أناس قد يلاقون من هؤلاء العمال ما لا يوافق أهواءهم، فيطعنون فيهم، ويتخذون من قرابتهم لعثمان وسيلة إلى الطعن في عثمان، فوجد فريقاً يوافقون أصحاب تلك الدعاية السرية في الطعن في عثمان نفسه، وإن كان الفريقان يختلفان في الباعث على هذا الطعن فأصحاب تلك الدعاية السرية يريدون تفريق كلمة المسلمين أو إفساد دينهم والفريق الثاني إنما يريد نقل الخلافة من عثمان إلى غيره، كراهة لبعض عماله أو رجاء أن يجد في خلافة غيره ولاية أو غنيمة وتكون من الفريقين جمع يتمضمضون بالطعن في عمال عثمان، ويتعدون بالطعن إلى عثمان نفسه، ينسبون إليه أشياء زوراً، ويذكرون بعض أعماله على غير وجهها الصحيح، وكان عثمان يقابل زعماء هذه الدعاية باللين ولا يزيد على أن يدفعهم بالحجة. كان جماعة من أهل الكوفة قد أظهروا العداء لعثمان فأبلغ سعيد بن العاص عثمان خبرهم فكتب إليه بإرسالهم إلى معاوية، وكتب إلى معاوية : إن نفراً خلقوا للفتنة، فقم عليهم، وانههم ، وإن أنست منهم رشداً فاقبل، وإن أعيوك فارددهم إلي، فأنزلهم معاوية، وأجرى عليهم من الرزق ما كان لهم بالعراق ولكن معاوية بعد محادثتهم، استصغر عقولهم، واحتقر شأنهم، وكتب إلى عثمان يقول له : إنه قدم عليّ أقوام ليس لهم عقول ولا أديان، أضجرهم العدل، لا يريدون الله بشيء، ولا يتكلمون بحجة، وإنما همهم الفتنة، وليسوا بالذين ينكون أحداً إلا مع غيرهم، فإنه سعيداً عنهم، فإنهم ليسوا لأكثر من شغب ونكير. ومما جعل عمال عثمان يوسعون صدورهم لهؤلاء الطاعنين، ولا يبادرون إلى عقوبتهم الزاجرة، أنهم كانوا يتظاهرون في طعنهم بحال من يريد الأمر بالمعروف والنهي عن المنكر. وقيام دعوة منظمة لا تهدأ ليلاً ولا نهاراً تختلق المعايب، وتلصقها بعثمان وعماله، وقد تأخذ بأذهان بعض الغافلين عن سريرة أولئك الدعاة، ويتخيلون أن الدعوة لإصلاح أمر الدولة، فيشارك هؤلاء الغافلون ذينك الفريقين في هذه الدعاية، أو يقفون في الأقل موقف الحيادة . فلا غرابة أن تنقل كلمات في نقد سياسة عثمان عن أناس لا يريدون إفساد حال المسلمين، ولا يبتغون إدراك منفعة خاصة قد فاتتهم وإنما يقولونها عن تأثر بتلك الدعاية المنظمة الدائبة. وربما ذكر المؤرخون أشخاصاً معدودين من الصحابة مثل عمّار بن ياسر وعمرو بن العاص، ويقولون : إنهم كانوا يؤلبون على عثمان، ومتى صح أصل الرواية، فمن المحتمل أن يكون الذي صدر منهم لا يزيد على إيذاء آراء يخالفون بها رأي عثمان في بعض تصرفات الدولة أو تولية رجال يرونهم غير ذي كفاية لما تقلدوا من الأعمال، فجاء بعض ذوي الأهواء إلى هذا النقد الذي لا تخلو منه دولة، وإن بلغت من الرشد والعدل غايتهما، وسماه تألباً وقد بلغ الحال بدعاة الفتنة أن يزوروا رسائل صدرت من عائشة وعلي وطلحة والزبير في الدعوة إلى خلع عثمان، وبلغ أمر هذه الرسائل إلى هؤلاء الصحابة الأجلاء وتبرأوا منها ، وأنكروا أن تكون صدرت منهم. وبمثل هذه الرسائل المزورة كانوا يخضعون الغافلين الذين لا يتثبتون فيما ينقل إليهم من الأنباء . والظاهر أن من أسباب سريان هذه الدعاية الخبيثة، كثرة من دخلوا في الإسلام ممن لم تستنر بصائرهم بهداية الدين الحنيف حق الاستنارة، ولم يقدروا أصحاب رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم حق أقدارهم، ويضاف إلى هذا ما كان عليه عثمان من النبل والحلم والحياء. ثم ما كان يجري عليه عماله من عدم مقابلة الطاعنين فيهم أو من عثمان بالشدة الزاجرة، إما استخفافاً بأمرهم وإما احتمالاً لهذه المطاعن، ولا سيما مطاعن يتظاهر أصحابها بأنهم يتظلمون أو يريدون إقامة معروف أو إزالة منكر . ومن تتبع سير الخلفاء الراشدين أو من جاء بعدهم من الخلفاء العاقلين، وجدهم لا يعاقبون الناس على نقد سياساتهم وإن ظهر النقد في أقوال جافية، وهذا معاوية يقول : والله لا أحمل السيف على من لا سيف له، فإن لم يكن من أحدهم إلا كلمة يشتفي بها جعلت له ذلك دبر أذني.
The Greater Imam Muhammad al-Khidr Husayn, Sheikh of al-Azhar, said under the title: How did the Fitna arise? Uthman spent most of his caliphate with the people united in love for him and delight in his leadership due to his intense compassion, vast forbearance, and gentleness, and because people's hands were filled with spoils in his era, and they enjoyed a good life more than they had. After this, a group of insincere people entered Islam, only wanting to plot against him and divide his community. Among them was Abdullah ibn Saba, known as Ibn al-Sawda. He was from the Jews of Himyar; he settled in Basra with Hakim ibn Jabala al-Abdi and began secretly spreading that Ali was more entitled to the caliphate, calling for the removal of Uthman. A group adhered to his call. Abdullah ibn Amir of Basra learned of his matter and expelled him. He came to Kufa and was expelled from there, then came to Syria and was expelled likewise. So he came to Egypt and contacted a group of the dregs of the people, among them [؟] ibn Bishr and Khalid ibn Muljam, and he kept repeating to them that Ali was the successor of the Prophet, and that Uthman had taken the caliphate unjustly. And he sent from these people preachers to the lands from which he had been expelled. It happened that Uthman had governors from his relatives, and there were people who would encounter from these governors what did not suit their desires, so they criticized them and used their relation to Uthman as a means to criticize Uthman himself. Thus he found a group that agreed with those of the secret propaganda in criticizing Uthman himself, although the two groups differed in motive: the secret propagandists wanted to divide the Muslim community or corrupt their religion, while the second group only wanted to transfer the caliphate from Uthman to another, out of dislike for some of his governors or hope of finding authority or booty under another's caliphate. From the two groups came a multitude who dripped with criticism of Uthman's governors and extended to criticism of Uthman himself, attributing false things to him and mentioning some of his actions incorrectly. Uthman met the leaders of this propaganda with gentleness and did no more than refute them with argument. A group from Kufa had shown enmity towards Uthman, so Sa'id ibn al-As informed Uthman of their news. Uthman wrote to him to send them to Mu'awiya, and wrote to Mu'awiya: 'Indeed, a group were created for fitna, so suppress them and forbid them; if you see from them rectitude, accept them; if they weary you, send them back to me.' Mu'awiya hosted them and provided them with the sustenance they had in Iraq. But Mu'awiya, after speaking with them, considered their intellects small and their matter contemptible, and wrote to Uthman saying: 'There have come to me people who have neither intellect nor religion; justice wearies them; they do not desire Allah in anything, nor do they speak with proof; their only concern is fitna. They are not such as to harm anyone except with others. So be pleased to be rid of them, for they are no more than noise and denial.' Among the reasons that made Uthman's governors broaden their chests toward these critics and not hasten to punish them deterrently was that they pretended in their criticism to be in a state of one who wants to enjoin good and forbid evil. And a organized call arose, not resting night or day, fabricating faults and attaching them to Uthman and his governors. It would take hold of the minds of some heedless people unaware of the secret of those preachers, and they imagined that the call was for reforming the state, so these heedless ones participated with those two groups in this propaganda, or at least adopted a neutral stance. So it is not surprising that words criticizing Uthman's policy were transmitted from people who did not want to corrupt the state of Muslims, nor sought to gain any personal benefit, but only spoke out of influence from that persistent organized propaganda. Historians may mention specific individuals from the Companions, such as Ammar ibn Yasir and Amr ibn al-As, and say that they were inciting against Uthman. If the origin of the report is authentic, it is probable that what came from them was no more than expressing opinions in which they disagreed with Uthman regarding some state actions or appointments of men they considered incompetent for the tasks they undertook. So some people of desires came to this criticism, which no state is free from, even if it reaches the utmost rectitude and justice, and called it incitement. The situation reached the point where the preachers of fitna forged letters purporting to come from Aisha, Ali, Talha, and al-Zubayr calling for the removal of Uthman. When news of these letters reached these eminent Companions, they disavowed them and denied that they had issued from them. With such forged letters they subdued the heedless who did not ascertain the news transmitted to them. It appears that among the reasons for the spread of this evil propaganda was the large number of those who had entered Islam whose insights had not been illuminated by the guidance of the true religion as they should have been, and who did not appreciate the Companions of the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, as they deserved. Added to this was what Uthman possessed of nobility, forbearance, and modesty. Then what his governors practiced of not confronting the critics—whether of them or of Uthman—with deterrent severity, either out of underestimation of their matter or out of tolerance for these criticisms, especially criticisms whose proponents pretended that they were complaining or wanted to establish good or remove evil. And whoever examines the conduct of the rightly-guided caliphs or the wise caliphs after them will find that they do not punish people for criticizing their policies, even if the criticism appears in harsh words. And Mu'awiya said: 'By Allah, I will not carry the sword against those who have no sword; if there is nothing from one of them but a word by which he finds relief, I let him have that behind my ear.'
Source pages p. 171

Commentary
This passage is a historical analysis by Muhammad al-Khidr Husayn of the origins of the fitna (civil strife) during Uthman's caliphate. It begins by noting the initial popularity of Uthman due to his kindness and prosperity. Then it describes the emergence of insincere converts, particularly Abdullah ibn Saba, a Jewish convert who secretly spread propaganda that Ali was the rightful caliph and that Uthman had usurped the position. Ibn Saba traveled to various cities, gathering followers and sending preachers. The passage distinguishes two groups of critics: the secret propagandists who aimed to divide the Muslims, and those who genuinely disliked Uthman's governors or hoped for personal gain under a new caliph. Both groups fueled criticism. Uthman and his governors responded with leniency, often tolerating criticism under the guise of 'enjoining good and forbidding evil.' The passage also discusses the role of some Companions like Ammar and Amr, suggesting their criticism was limited to policy disagreements, not outright rebellion. It highlights the use of forged letters attributed to prominent Companions to stir up opposition. Finally, it notes that the spread of fitna was due to weak faith among new converts and the lenient policy of the caliphs, who did not punish criticism harshly, as exemplified by Mu'awiya's statement.

Key Terms
الفتنة
عبد الله بن سبأ
الدعاية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Uthman's rule was unjust from the start.
Correction: The passage shows that Uthman was initially loved and the opposition was orchestrated by insincere converts like Ibn Saba.

Checkpoint
Who was the main instigator of the fitna according to this passage?
A) Ammar ibn Yasir
B) Abdullah ibn Saba
C) Muawiya
D) The people of Kufa

Key Takeaway
Abdullah ibn Saba's secret propaganda was the initial spark of the fitna against Uthman.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear a story that accuses a leader of injustice, do you pause to ask who is spreading it and for what purpose, or do you accept it easily? How does Ibn Saba's method of secret propaganda challenge you to be more discerning about information?

Sects and Disagreements
beginner
6 min
The Two Groups of Critics and Uthman's Leniency
Classification of critics into two groups and Uthman's lenient policy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two distinct groups that criticized Uthman and how his lenient response contributed to the growth of the fitna.

Core Idea
Two groups of critics, one malicious and one with grievances, exploited Uthman's leniency.

This lesson explores the dynamics of opposition during Uthman's caliphate. The author distinguishes between two groups: the secret propagandists who aimed to divide the community, and those who genuinely disliked Uthman's governors or hoped for personal gain. We will also see how Uthman and his governors responded with leniency, even when faced with harsh criticism.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the two groups
Read the Arabic passage focusing on the distinction between the two groups of critics. Note their different motives.
The passage clearly separates 'secret propagandists' from those who wanted to replace Uthman for worldly reasons.
2
Examine Uthman's response
Observe how Uthman dealt with the leaders of the propaganda: with gentleness and argument, not force. Also note the correspondence with Muawiya.
Uthman writes to Muawiya about a group from Kufa, and Muawiya's reply reveals his assessment of them.
3
Reflect on the consequences
Consider how this leniency allowed the fitna to escalate. The author implies that a firmer response might have prevented the crisis.
Muawiya describes the group as having 'neither intellect nor religion'.

Source Text
