كيف دبر خلع عثمان أو قتله : مما لا نرتاب فيه أن ليس للصحابة ولا لأفاضل التابعين سعي في خلع عثمان، ولا دخل في قتله، وأن المؤتمرون على ذلك دعاة الفتنة، واستعانوا بمن تلون بدعايتهم ، ونعول في هذا على أقوال المحدثين والمحققين من المؤرخين، قال الحافظ أبو بكر العربي في كتاب القواصم والعواصم : وقد سموا من قام على عثمان، فوجدناهم أهل أغراض سوء، حيل بينهم وبينها، وقال: إن أحداً من الصحابة لم يشنع عليه، وقد انتدب المردة الجهلة أن يقولوا: إن كل فاضل من الصحابة كان عليه مشاغباً مؤلباً، وبما جرى عليه راضياً، واخترعوا كتباً فيها فصاحة وأمثال، وادعوا أن عثمان كتب بها إلى علي، وذلك كله مصنوع، ليوغروا قلوب المسلمين على السلف الماضين والخلفاء الراشدين. اجتمع بعض رؤوس الفتنة بالكوفة، وأخذوا يزيدون نارها حطباً، فكتب سعيد بن العاص يشكوهم إلى عثمان، فأمره بإرسالهم إلى عبد الرحمن بن خالد عامل حمص فوتخهم ابن خالد وتوعدهم فها بوا سطوته، وأظهروا التوبة وأرسل بهم إلى عثمان متظاهرين بالتوبة، فخيرهـم عثمان بالبلاد التي يريدون استيطانها، فاختاروا التفرق، وذهب كل إلى البلد الذي اختاره ولما ســار كـل إلى مــا اختار، عادوا إلى إيقاد الفتنة وتأليب الجماعة، وتكاتبوا من أمصارهم في القدوم على المدينة، حتى جمعوا أمرهم وعزموا على خلع عثمان أو قتله، وتوجهوا نحو المدينة، متظاهرين بقصد الحج، كان على أهل البصرة حكيم بن جبلة، وعلى أهل الكوفة الأشتر النخعي وعلى أهل مصر عبد الرحمن بن عديس البلوي فدخلوا المدينة في نحو أربعة آلاف شخص، فاطلع عليهم عثمان داره ووعظهم وذكرهم، فاستشاطوا ولم تنجع فيهم الموعظة، وأراد الصحابة أن يدفعوهم عنه، فأوعز إليهم عثمان أن لا يقاتل أحد بسببه أبداً، وثبت أن عبد الله بن الزبير قال لعثمان: إن معك في الدار عصابة مستبصرة، ينصر الله بأقل منها، فأذن لنا، فقال: اذكر الله رجلاً أراق لي دماً. وقال سليط بن سليط نهانا عثمان عن قتالهم، ولو أذن لنا لضربناهم حتى نخرجهم من أقطارنا. وجاء زيد بن ثابت فقال له : إن هؤلاء الأنصار بالباب يقولون : إن شئت كنا أنصار الله مرتين، قال: لا حاجة لي ذلك، كفوا. وروي أن عبد الله بن عامر قال: كنت مع بن عامر قال: كنت مع عثمان في الدار فقال لي: اعزم على كل من رأى أن عليه سمعاً وطاعة إلا كف يده وسلاحه، ويحدثنا القاضي أبو بكر في كتابه ( العارضة ) فيقول: ولقد قتل عثمان، وطالبوه أربعة آلاف وفي المدينة أربعون ألفاً كلهم لا يريد قتله، ويريد نصره، لكنه دفع الكل، واستسلم للأمر بالعهد الذي كان عنده، ولم يرض أن يراق بسببه دم ورضي أن يكون عند الله المظلوم ولا يكون عند الله الظالم. ولما ضرب أولئك البغاة على عثمان الحصر، كان معه وعلى بابه جماعة من الصحابة وأبناء الصحابة يحرسونه، منهم زيد بن ثابت وأبو هريرة وعبد الله بن عمر والحسن والحسين وعبد الله ابن الزبير [؟] الله بن عامر، وربما وقعت بينهم وبين الثائرين مدافعة، حتى أصيب الحسن [؟] وطلحة [؟] وعبد [؟] ومحمد بن [؟] وغيره بجراح. ثم إن هؤلاء الثائرين اقتحموا دار عثمان يريدون قتله. ويذكر المؤرخون في أسماء من باشروا قتله محمد بن أبي بكر الصديق، ومحمد بن أبي بكر لم يكن من الصحابة لأنه ولد سنة حجة الوداع، وهي السنة التي انتقل عقبها النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم إلى الرفيق الأعلى، فكان أيام فتنة عثمان لم يزل في أوائل الشباب على أن بعض الروايات تقول: إن محمد بن أبي بكر بعد أن دخل على عثمان كلّمه ووعظه فرجع، ثم دخل سفهاء القوم، فسفكوا دمه الطاهر وكتاب الله بين يديه وصعدت روحه الطاهرة إلى مقام كريم.
How the removal of Uthman or his killing was planned: There is no doubt for us that there was no effort by the Companions or the eminent Successors in the removal of Uthman, nor involvement in his killing, and that those who conspired for that were the callers of sedition, and they sought help from those who were colored by their propaganda. We rely in this on the sayings of the hadith scholars and the verifying historians. Al-Hafiz Abu Bakr al-Arabi said in his book al-Qawasim wa al-Awasim: 'They named those who rose against Uthman, and we found them to be people of evil intentions, but they were prevented from attaining them.' He said: 'None of the Companions rebuked him, but the ignorant rebels claimed that every virtuous Companion was quarrelsome and inciting against him, and pleased with what happened to him, and they fabricated eloquent books and claimed that Uthman wrote them to Ali, all of which is forged, in order to embitter the hearts of Muslims against the past predecessors and the rightly guided caliphs.' Some heads of sedition gathered in Kufa and began adding fuel to the fire. Sa'id ibn al-As wrote to Uthman complaining about them, so he ordered him to send them to Abd al-Rahman ibn Khalid, the governor of Hims. Ibn Khalid intimidated them and threatened them, so they were awed by his power, showed repentance, and were sent back to Uthman pretending to repent. Uthman gave them the choice of the lands they wished to settle, so they chose to disperse, and each went to the land he chose. But when each went to what he chose, they returned to kindling sedition and inciting the community, and they corresponded from their provinces to come to Medina, until they consolidated their affair and resolved to remove Uthman or kill him. They headed toward Medina pretending to intend the pilgrimage. In charge of the Basrans was Hakim ibn Jabalah, in charge of the Kufans was al-Ashtar al-Nakha'i, and in charge of the Egyptians was Abd al-Rahman ibn Adis al-Balawi. They entered Medina with about four thousand people. Uthman looked out at them from his house, admonished them, and reminded them, but they became furious and the admonition did not avail them. The Companions wanted to repel them from him, but Uthman instructed them that no one should ever fight on his account. It is confirmed that Abd Allah ibn al-Zubayr said to Uthman: 'With you in the house is a discerning group; Allah will grant victory with fewer than them, so permit us.' He said: 'I remind you of Allah, a man who would spill blood for me.' Sulayt ibn Sulayt said: 'Uthman forbade us from fighting them. If he had permitted us, we would have struck them until we expelled them from our regions.' Zayd ibn Thabit came to him and said: 'These Ansar are at the door saying: If you wish, we will be the helpers of Allah twice.' He said: 'I have no need of that; refrain.' It is narrated that Abd Allah ibn Amir said: 'I was with Ibn Amir... I was with Uthman in the house, and he said to me: I adjure everyone who considers it obligatory upon him to hear and obey to withhold his hand and weapon.' And al-Qadi Abu Bakr tells us in his book al-Arida: 'Uthman was killed while his demanders were four thousand, and in Medina were forty thousand, none of whom wanted to kill him, and wanted to support him, but he repelled them all, surrendered to the matter due to the covenant he had, and was not willing that blood be shed because of him. He was content to be the oppressed with Allah and not to be the oppressor with Allah.' When those rebels besieged Uthman, there were with him at his door a group of Companions and sons of Companions guarding him, among them Zayd ibn Thabit, Abu Hurayra, Abd Allah ibn Umar, al-Hasan, al-Husayn, Abd Allah ibn al-Zubayr, [؟] Allah ibn Amir, and sometimes there occurred between them and the rebels a scuffle, until al-Hasan [؟] and Talha [؟] and Abd [؟] and Muhammad ibn [؟] and others were wounded. Then these rebels stormed the house of Uthman intending to kill him. The historians mention among the names of those who directly participated in his killing Muhammad ibn Abi Bakr al-Siddiq. Muhammad ibn Abi Bakr was not from the Companions because he was born in the year of the Farewell Pilgrimage, which was the year after which the Prophet, peace and blessings be upon him, passed to the Most High Companion. So during the days of the sedition of Uthman, he was still in early youth, although some narrations say that Muhammad ibn Abi Bakr, after entering upon Uthman, spoke with him and admonished him and then withdrew. Then the foolish ones of the people entered and shed his pure blood while the Book of Allah was before him, and his pure soul ascended to a noble station.
Source pages p. 173

Commentary
This passage is a historical narrative defending the Companions of the Prophet from any involvement in the murder of Caliph Uthman. The author begins by stating emphatically that there is no doubt that neither the Companions nor the eminent Successors had any part in plotting the removal or killing of Uthman. Instead, those who conspired were 'the callers of sedition' (du'at al-fitna). The author relies on the words of hadith scholars and historians, specifically quoting al-Hafiz Abu Bakr al-Arabi. Al-Arabi states that those who rose against Uthman were people of evil intentions, but they were prevented from achieving their goals. He further asserts that no Companion rebuked Uthman, but the ignorant rebels fabricated books falsely attributed to Uthman and Ali in order to incite hatred among Muslims against the early generations. The narrative then describes the origin of the rebellion: some heads of sedition gathered in Kufa and were sent to the governor of Hims, who intimidated them into showing repentance. They were then sent to Uthman, who allowed them to choose where to settle. They dispersed but soon resumed their subversive activities, corresponding with each other to march on Medina. They gathered about four thousand men from Basra, Kufa, and Egypt, pretending to go on pilgrimage. Uthman addressed them from his house but they were unmoved. The Companions wanted to fight them, but Uthman forbade them absolutely, recounting several incidents where he refused offers of defense: Abd Allah ibn al-Zubayr offered to fight with a small group, but Uthman reminded him of Allah regarding shedding blood; Sulayt ibn Sulayt said Uthman forbade them; Zayd ibn Thabit offered the help of the Ansar but Uthman declined; and Abd Allah ibn Amir reported that Uthman adjured everyone to withhold their hands. The author then quotes al-Qadi Abu Bakr who observes that while four thousand besieged Uthman, forty thousand in Medina did not want to kill him and wished to support him, but Uthman rejected all help, surrendering to his fate and preferring to be the oppressed rather than the oppressor. During the siege, several Companions and their sons guarded Uthman's door, including Zayd ibn Thabit, Abu Hurayra, Abd Allah ibn Umar, al-Hasan, al-Husayn, Abd Allah ibn al-Zubayr, and others. Some scuffles occurred, and some were wounded. The passage concludes with the storming of the house and the killing of Uthman. The author notes that Muhammad ibn Abi Bakr, though named among the killers, was not a Companion because he was born in the year of the Farewell Pilgrimage. According to some reports, Muhammad ibn Abi Bakr entered, spoke with Uthman, and then withdrew, and the actual killing was done by the foolish ones. Thus the narrative consistently absolves the Companions and places blame on the seditious rebels.

Key Terms
الفتنة
الكوفة
حمص
المدينة
الحج

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The rebellion was a spontaneous popular uprising.
Correction: The passage shows it was orchestrated by specific leaders who had previously pretended to repent and then coordinated from different provinces.

Checkpoint
How did the rebels initially respond when sent to the governor of Hims?
A) They attacked him.
B) They showed repentance and were awed by him.
C) They escaped.
D) They wrote to Uthman protesting.

Key Takeaway
The rebellion against Uthman was carefully planned by a small group of seditionists who used deception and coordinated from multiple provinces.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever pretended to change or repent outwardly while your heart remained stubborn? What would it take for you to truly humble yourself before Allah and others, even when you feel angry or defensive?
?
Uthman did not use force against the rebels; he admonished them gently. When someone corrects you, especially if you know they are right, do you react with fury like the rebels, or do you pause and consider the truth? Ask yourself: What prevents me from accepting sincere advice?

Sects and Disagreements
beginner
6 min
Uthman's Martyrdom and the Companions' Defense
Narrative of Uthman's refusal to fight and the final siege.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Uthman refused to allow his Companions to fight, preferring martyrdom over bloodshed, and that the actual killing was carried out by a small group of rebels, not by any Companion.

Core Idea
Uthman chose to be the oppressed rather than the oppressor.

This lesson focuses on the tragic climax of the siege. Despite the presence of many Companions and their offers to fight, Uthman repeatedly forbade any violence in his defense. The narrative provides multiple examples of Companions wanting to protect him and his steadfast refusal. It also clarifies that Muhammad ibn Abi Bakr, though present, was not a Companion and ultimately withdrew, while the actual killing was done by the foolish ones. The lesson highlights Uthman's piety and the Companions' loyalty.

Guided Path
1
Notice Uthman's repeated refusals
Track the different requests: from Abd Allah ibn al-Zubayr, Sulayt ibn Sulayt, Zayd ibn Thabit, and Abd Allah ibn Amir. Each time Uthman forbids fighting.
This shows his determination to avoid bloodshed.
2
Reflect on the Companions' offers
The Companions were willing to fight, but Uthman prevented them. This proves their innocence and loyalty.
3
Understand the role of Muhammad ibn Abi Bakr
The author clarifies that he was not a Companion and that he left after admonishing Uthman. The killers were the foolish ones.
This counters any accusation against the family of Abu Bakr.
4
Appreciate the final scene
Uthman was killed while reciting the Quran, accepting his fate as the oppressed.

كيف دبر خلع عثمان أو قتله : مما لا نرتاب فيه أن ليس للصحابة ولا لأفاضل التابعين سعي في خلع عثمان، ولا دخل في قتله، وأن المؤتمرون على ذلك دعاة الفتنة، واستعانوا بمن تلون بدعايتهم ، ونعول في هذا على أقوال المحدثين والمحققين من المؤرخين، قال الحافظ أبو بكر العربي في كتاب القواصم والعواصم : وقد سموا من قام على عثمان، فوجدناهم أهل أغراض سوء، حيل بينهم وبينها، وقال: إن أحداً من الصحابة لم يشنع عليه، وقد انتدب المردة الجهلة أن يقولوا: إن كل فاضل من الصحابة كان عليه مشاغباً مؤلباً، وبما جرى عليه راضياً، واخترعوا كتباً فيها فصاحة وأمثال، وادعوا أن عثمان كتب بها إلى علي، وذلك كله مصنوع، ليوغروا قلوب المسلمين على السلف الماضين والخلفاء الراشدين. اجتمع بعض رؤوس الفتنة بالكوفة، وأخذوا يزيدون نارها حطباً، فكتب سعيد بن العاص يشكوهم إلى عثمان، فأمره بإرسالهم إلى عبد الرحمن بن خالد عامل حمص فوتخهم ابن خالد وتوعدهم فها بوا سطوته، وأظهروا التوبة وأرسل بهم إلى عثمان متظاهرين بالتوبة، فخيرهـم عثمان بالبلاد التي يريدون استيطانها، فاختاروا التفرق، وذهب كل إلى البلد الذي اختاره ولما ســار كـل إلى مــا اختار، عادوا إلى إيقاد الفتنة وتأليب الجماعة، وتكاتبوا من أمصارهم في القدوم على المدينة، حتى جمعوا أمرهم وعزموا على خلع عثمان أو قتله، وتوجهوا نحو المدينة، متظاهرين بقصد الحج، كان على أهل البصرة حكيم بن جبلة، وعلى أهل الكوفة الأشتر النخعي وعلى أهل مصر عبد الرحمن بن عديس البلوي فدخلوا المدينة في نحو أربعة آلاف شخص، فاطلع عليهم عثمان داره ووعظهم وذكرهم، فاستشاطوا ولم تنجع فيهم الموعظة، وأراد الصحابة أن يدفعوهم عنه، فأوعز إليهم عثمان أن لا يقاتل أحد بسببه أبداً، وثبت أن عبد الله بن الزبير قال لعثمان: إن معك في الدار عصابة مستبصرة، ينصر الله بأقل منها، فأذن لنا، فقال: اذكر الله رجلاً أراق لي دماً. وقال سليط بن سليط نهانا عثمان عن قتالهم، ولو أذن لنا لضربناهم حتى نخرجهم من أقطارنا. وجاء زيد بن ثابت فقال له : إن هؤلاء الأنصار بالباب يقولون : إن شئت كنا أنصار الله مرتين، قال: لا حاجة لي ذلك، كفوا. وروي أن عبد الله بن عامر قال: كنت مع بن عامر قال: كنت مع عثمان في الدار فقال لي: اعزم على كل من رأى أن عليه سمعاً وطاعة إلا كف يده وسلاحه، ويحدثنا القاضي أبو بكر في كتابه ( العارضة ) فيقول: ولقد قتل عثمان، وطالبوه أربعة آلاف وفي المدينة أربعون ألفاً كلهم لا يريد قتله، ويريد نصره، لكنه دفع الكل، واستسلم للأمر بالعهد الذي كان عنده، ولم يرض أن يراق بسببه دم ورضي أن يكون عند الله المظلوم ولا يكون عند الله الظالم. ولما ضرب أولئك البغاة على عثمان الحصر، كان معه وعلى بابه جماعة من الصحابة وأبناء الصحابة يحرسونه، منهم زيد بن ثابت وأبو هريرة وعبد الله بن عمر والحسن والحسين وعبد الله ابن الزبير [؟] الله بن عامر، وربما وقعت بينهم وبين الثائرين مدافعة، حتى أصيب الحسن [؟] وطلحة [؟] وعبد [؟] ومحمد بن [؟] وغيره بجراح. ثم إن هؤلاء الثائرين اقتحموا دار عثمان يريدون قتله. ويذكر المؤرخون في أسماء من باشروا قتله محمد بن أبي بكر الصديق، ومحمد بن أبي بكر لم يكن من الصحابة لأنه ولد سنة حجة الوداع، وهي السنة التي انتقل عقبها النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم إلى الرفيق الأعلى، فكان أيام فتنة عثمان لم يزل في أوائل الشباب على أن بعض الروايات تقول: إن محمد بن أبي بكر بعد أن دخل على عثمان كلّمه ووعظه فرجع، ثم دخل سفهاء القوم، فسفكوا دمه الطاهر وكتاب الله بين يديه وصعدت روحه الطاهرة إلى مقام كريم.
How the removal of Uthman or his killing was planned: There is no doubt for us that there was no effort by the Companions or the eminent Successors in the removal of Uthman, nor involvement in his killing, and that those who conspired for that were the callers of sedition, and they sought help from those who were colored by their propaganda. We rely in this on the sayings of the hadith scholars and the verifying historians. Al-Hafiz Abu Bakr al-Arabi said in his book al-Qawasim wa al-Awasim: 'They named those who rose against Uthman, and we found them to be people of evil intentions, but they were prevented from attaining them.' He said: 'None of the Companions rebuked him, but the ignorant rebels claimed that every virtuous Companion was quarrelsome and inciting against him, and pleased with what happened to him, and they fabricated eloquent books and claimed that Uthman wrote them to Ali, all of which is forged, in order to embitter the hearts of Muslims against the past predecessors and the rightly guided caliphs.' Some heads of sedition gathered in Kufa and began adding fuel to the fire. Sa'id ibn al-As wrote to Uthman complaining about them, so he ordered him to send them to Abd al-Rahman ibn Khalid, the governor of Hims. Ibn Khalid intimidated them and threatened them, so they were awed by his power, showed repentance, and were sent back to Uthman pretending to repent. Uthman gave them the choice of the lands they wished to settle, so they chose to disperse, and each went to the land he chose. But when each went to what he chose, they returned to kindling sedition and inciting the community, and they corresponded from their provinces to come to Medina, until they consolidated their affair and resolved to remove Uthman or kill him. They headed toward Medina pretending to intend the pilgrimage. In charge of the Basrans was Hakim ibn Jabalah, in charge of the Kufans was al-Ashtar al-Nakha'i, and in charge of the Egyptians was Abd al-Rahman ibn Adis al-Balawi. They entered Medina with about four thousand people. Uthman looked out at them from his house, admonished them, and reminded them, but they became furious and the admonition did not avail them. The Companions wanted to repel them from him, but Uthman instructed them that no one should ever fight on his account. It is confirmed that Abd Allah ibn al-Zubayr said to Uthman: 'With you in the house is a discerning group; Allah will grant victory with fewer than them, so permit us.' He said: 'I remind you of Allah, a man who would spill blood for me.' Sulayt ibn Sulayt said: 'Uthman forbade us from fighting them. If he had permitted us, we would have struck them until we expelled them from our regions.' Zayd ibn Thabit came to him and said: 'These Ansar are at the door saying: If you wish, we will be the helpers of Allah twice.' He said: 'I have no need of that; refrain.' It is narrated that Abd Allah ibn Amir said: 'I was with Ibn Amir... I was with Uthman in the house, and he said to me: I adjure everyone who considers it obligatory upon him to hear and obey to withhold his hand and weapon.' And al-Qadi Abu Bakr tells us in his book al-Arida: 'Uthman was killed while his demanders were four thousand, and in Medina were forty thousand, none of whom wanted to kill him, and wanted to support him, but he repelled them all, surrendered to the matter due to the covenant he had, and was not willing that blood be shed because of him. He was content to be the oppressed with Allah and not to be the oppressor with Allah.' When those rebels besieged Uthman, there were with him at his door a group of Companions and sons of Companions guarding him, among them Zayd ibn Thabit, Abu Hurayra, Abd Allah ibn Umar, al-Hasan, al-Husayn, Abd Allah ibn al-Zubayr, [؟] Allah ibn Amir, and sometimes there occurred between them and the rebels a scuffle, until al-Hasan [؟] and Talha [؟] and Abd [؟] and Muhammad ibn [؟] and others were wounded. Then these rebels stormed the house of Uthman intending to kill him. The historians mention among the names of those who directly participated in his killing Muhammad ibn Abi Bakr al-Siddiq. Muhammad ibn Abi Bakr was not from the Companions because he was born in the year of the Farewell Pilgrimage, which was the year after which the Prophet, peace and blessings be upon him, passed to the Most High Companion. So during the days of the sedition of Uthman, he was still in early youth, although some narrations say that Muhammad ibn Abi Bakr, after entering upon Uthman, spoke with him and admonished him and then withdrew. Then the foolish ones of the people entered and shed his pure blood while the Book of Allah was before him, and his pure soul ascended to a noble station.
Source pages p. 173

Commentary
This passage is a historical narrative defending the Companions of the Prophet from any involvement in the murder of Caliph Uthman. The author begins by stating emphatically that there is no doubt that neither the Companions nor the eminent Successors had any part in plotting the removal or killing of Uthman. Instead, those who conspired were 'the callers of sedition' (du'at al-fitna). The author relies on the words of hadith scholars and historians, specifically quoting al-Hafiz Abu Bakr al-Arabi. Al-Arabi states that those who rose against Uthman were people of evil intentions, but they were prevented from achieving their goals. He further asserts that no Companion rebuked Uthman, but the ignorant rebels fabricated books falsely attributed to Uthman and Ali in order to incite hatred among Muslims against the early generations. The narrative then describes the origin of the rebellion: some heads of sedition gathered in Kufa and were sent to the governor of Hims, who intimidated them into showing repentance. They were then sent to Uthman, who allowed them to choose where to settle. They dispersed but soon resumed their subversive activities, corresponding with each other to march on Medina. They gathered about four thousand men from Basra, Kufa, and Egypt, pretending to go on pilgrimage. Uthman addressed them from his house but they were unmoved. The Companions wanted to fight them, but Uthman forbade them absolutely, recounting several incidents where he refused offers of defense: Abd Allah ibn al-Zubayr offered to fight with a small group, but Uthman reminded him of Allah regarding shedding blood; Sulayt ibn Sulayt said Uthman forbade them; Zayd ibn Thabit offered the help of the Ansar but Uthman declined; and Abd Allah ibn Amir reported that Uthman adjured everyone to withhold their hands. The author then quotes al-Qadi Abu Bakr who observes that while four thousand besieged Uthman, forty thousand in Medina did not want to kill him and wished to support him, but Uthman rejected all help, surrendering to his fate and preferring to be the oppressed rather than the oppressor. During the siege, several Companions and their sons guarded Uthman's door, including Zayd ibn Thabit, Abu Hurayra, Abd Allah ibn Umar, al-Hasan, al-Husayn, Abd Allah ibn al-Zubayr, and others. Some scuffles occurred, and some were wounded. The passage concludes with the storming of the house and the killing of Uthman. The author notes that Muhammad ibn Abi Bakr, though named among the killers, was not a Companion because he was born in the year of the Farewell Pilgrimage. According to some reports, Muhammad ibn Abi Bakr entered, spoke with Uthman, and then withdrew, and the actual killing was done by the foolish ones. Thus the narrative consistently absolves the Companions and places blame on the seditious rebels.

الحسين
محمد بن أبي بكر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Muhammad ibn Abi Bakr, a Companion, killed Uthman.
Correction: Muhammad ibn Abi Bakr was not a Companion (born after the Prophet's death) and, according to some reports, left after admonishing Uthman; the killing was done by the foolish ones.

Checkpoint
Why did Uthman refuse the help of the Companions?
A) He thought they were weak.
B) He did not want to spill blood on his account.
C) He planned to negotiate.
D) He was afraid of civil war.

Key Takeaway
Uthman preferred martyrdom over bloodshed, and the Companions were innocent of his killing.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When have you been in a situation where you had the power to fight back but chose restraint? How did that choice reflect your faith in Allah?
?
Is there an injustice you are currently facing where you are tempted to retaliate? How does Uthman's example challenge you to prefer being the oppressed rather than the oppressor?
?
What would it cost you personally to surrender your rights for the sake of avoiding bloodshed, as Uthman did? Are you willing to pay that price?

Sects and Disagreements

Categorizing the Accusations Against Uthman: Principles of Ijtihad
The author categorizes the accusations and states the general rebuttal principle.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author categorizes the accusations against Uthman into three types and the principle that appointing governors is a matter of ijtihad, not nepotism.

Core Idea
Accusations against Uthman are either fabricated, matters of ijtihad, or good deeds; appointment is a matter of ijtihad.

This lesson examines the first part of the defense of Caliph Uthman. The author categorizes the criticisms into three types: fabrications, matters of ijtihad, and good deeds. Then he presents the specific accusation of appointing relatives and gives a general rebuttal based on the principle that the imam's appointments are based on ijtihad and competence, not favoritism.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three categories
Read the opening sentences where the author categorizes the accusations: some are fabricated, some are matters of ijtihad, some are good deeds.
This sets the framework for the defense.
2
Understand the main accusation
The historians claim Uthman appointed unfit relatives. List the names mentioned.
Note that the author will address each name later.
3
Grasp the rebuttal principle
The author argues that appointments are ijtihad, and Uthman's piety ensures he only appointed competent relatives.
This is the core argument against nepotism.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
رد ما ينسب إلى عثمان من الأحداث : يذكر المؤرخون أشياء كان الناقمون على عثمان قد اتخذوها أسباباً لثورتهم عليه، ومن هذه الأشياء ما هو مفترى على عثمان قطعاً، ومنها لو صح لم يكن موضع إنكار ، وإنما هو من قبيل ما يرجع إلى اجتهاد الإمام، ويقع مثله من الخلفاء الراشدين، ومنها ما يعد من حسناته وصالح أعماله. وها نحن هؤلاء نعرض على حضراتكم ما قصه المؤرخون وبعض المحدثين من الأمور التي طعن بها الطاعنون في عثمان، وجعلوها أسباب قيامهم عليه : قالوا: ولى عمالاً من ذوي قرابته، وزعموا أنهم ليسوا أهلاً للولاية، وذكروا معاوية بن أبي سفيان والوليد بن عقبة وعبد الله بن سعد بن أبي سرح، وسعيد بن العاص، وعبد الله بن عامر، ومروان بن الحكم. ويدفع هذا بأن تعيين الولاة يرجع إلى اجتهاد الإمام، وتقوى عثمان وإخلاصه في سياسة الرعية، يجعلنا على ثقة من أنه لو ولّى بعض ذوي قرابته بعد أن عرف كفايتهم للأعمال، والمعيب أن يولي قريباً لا يكون كافياً للعمل، أو يؤثره في الولاية وهو على علم بأن غيره أكفى منه، ثم إن معاوية ولاه الشام عمر بن الخطاب، ولم يزد عثمان على أن أقره على الولاية، وكذلك الوليد بـن عقبة كان عاملاً لعمر بن الخطاب على الجزيرة، وكان من عثمان أن ولاه الكوفة، فقدمها وسار في الناس خمس سنين سيرة حسنة، حتى اتهمه جماعة بشرب الخمر فاستقدمه عثمان وأقام عليه الحد، وولى مكانه سعيد بن العاص، وسعيد بن العاص نشأ يتيماً في حجر عثمان، ثم انتقل إلى الشام، وأقام بها عند معاوية، فذكره عمر بن الخطاب يوماً، واستقدمه إلى المدينة وأكرمه، وكان شريف النفس سخي اليد فصيح اللسان لا يختلف اثنان في كفايته للعمل الله وأما عبد بن عامر بن كريز، فكان ابن خال عثمان وأمه أم حكيم ابنة عبد المطلب، عمة النبي ، وعبد الله بن عامر هذا نشأ في الإسلام نشأة طيبة، وكان معدوداً من نجباء قريش وكرمائهم، ولاه عثمان عاملاً بالبصرة عند اختلاف أهلها على أبي موسى الأشعري، وكان سن عبد الله بن عامر يومئذ خمساً وعشرين سنة فقاد الجيوش، وفتح خراسان وسجستان وكرمان، ومازال يطارد كسرى يزدجرد حتى قتل كسرى وانقرضت على يده الدولة الساسانية، وكان لكرمه وحسن خلقه يحبه الناس.
Refutation of what is attributed to Uthman of events: The historians mention things that the critics of Uthman had taken as reasons for their revolt against him. Among these things are what is definitely fabricated against Uthman, and among them, even if true, would not be a matter of denial, but rather are of the type that go back to the ijtihad of the Imam, and similar occurs from the rightly guided caliphs, and among them are things that count among his good deeds and righteous works. Now we present to you what the historians and some hadith scholars have narrated of the matters by which the critics reviled Uthman and made them causes for their rising against him: They said: He appointed governors from among his relatives, and they claimed that they were not fit for governance, and they mentioned Muawiya ibn Abi Sufyan, al-Walid ibn Uqba, Abd Allah ibn Sa'd ibn Abi Sarh, Sa'id ibn al-As, Abd Allah ibn Amir, and Marwan ibn al-Hakam. This is rebutted by the fact that the appointment of governors goes back to the ijtihad of the Imam. The piety of Uthman and his sincerity in administering the subjects makes us confident that if he appointed some of his relatives, it was after he knew their competence for the work. The blameworthy is to appoint a relative who is not competent for the work, or to prefer him in governance while knowing that another is more competent than him. Moreover, Muawiya was appointed over Syria by Umar ibn al-Khattab, and Uthman only confirmed him in the governorship. Similarly, al-Walid ibn Uqba was a governor for Umar ibn al-Khattab over al-Jazira, and it was from Uthman that he appointed him over Kufa. He came to Kufa and conducted himself among the people for five years with good conduct, until a group accused him of drinking wine, so Uthman summoned him and carried out the prescribed punishment on him, and appointed Sa'id ibn al-As in his place. Sa'id ibn al-As grew up as an orphan in the care of Uthman, then moved to Syria and stayed there with Muawiya. Umar ibn al-Khattab mentioned him one day, summoned him to Medina, and honored him. He was noble in spirit, generous of hand, eloquent of tongue; no two persons differed about his competence for the work. As for Abd Allah ibn Amir ibn Kurayz, he was the maternal cousin of Uthman, his mother was Umm Hakim bint Abd al-Muttalib, the aunt of the Prophet. This Abd Allah ibn Amir grew up in Islam with a good upbringing, and was counted among the cleverest and most generous of Quraysh. Uthman appointed him as governor of Basra when its people differed over Abu Musa al-Ash'ari. At that time Abd Allah ibn Amir was twenty-five years old. He led armies, conquered Khurasan, Sijistan, and Kirman, and continued to pursue Chosroes Yazdegerd until he killed him and the Sassanid empire came to an end at his hands. Because of his generosity and good character, people loved him.
Source pages p. 174

Commentary
This passage is a refutation (radd) of the accusations leveled against Caliph Uthman, specifically the claim that he appointed his relatives to governorships while they were unqualified. The author begins by categorizing the criticisms: some are outright fabrications, some if true would not be blameworthy because they fall under the ijtihad (independent reasoning) of the Imam and similar actions occurred from the other rightly guided caliphs, and some are actually among Uthman's good deeds. The main accusation presented is that Uthman appointed governors from his relatives, naming Muawiya ibn Abi Sufyan, al-Walid ibn Uqba, Abd Allah ibn Sa'd ibn Abi Sarh, Sa'id ibn al-As, Abd Allah ibn Amir, and Marwan ibn al-Hakam. The author then provides a three-part rebuttal. First, he states a general principle: the appointment of governors is a matter of ijtihad, and Uthman's piety and sincerity give us confidence that he only appointed relatives after verifying their competence. The blameworthy act would be to appoint an incompetent relative, not to appoint a competent one. Second, he addresses each named governor individually: Muawiya was originally appointed by Umar, so Uthman merely confirmed him. Al-Walid ibn Uqba was also a governor under Umar; Uthman appointed him to Kufa, where he had a good record for five years, and when he was accused of drinking, Uthman applied the legal punishment and replaced him with Sa'id ibn al-As. Sa'id ibn al-As, though raised by Uthman, was recognized by Umar as competent and was honored by him. Abd Allah ibn Amir was also competent: he was of noble character, appointed at a young age, and he conquered vast territories and ended the Sassanid empire. Thus, each governor was either appointed by Umar or proven competent by their actions. The defense relies on historical precedent and the character of the individuals, concluding that the accusation of nepotism is unfounded.

Key Terms
الولاة
الاجتهاد
الخلفاء الراشدون

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All accusations against Uthman are true and he was guilty of nepotism.
Correction: The passage shows some accusations are fabricated, some are matters of ijtihad, and some are good deeds. Uthman appointed relatives with competence, not for favoritism.

Checkpoint
How does the author categorize the accusations against Uthman?
A) All are fabricated.
B) They are of three types: fabricated, matters of ijtihad, and good deeds.
C) All are true but excusable.
D) Only some are political.

Key Takeaway
The author classifies accusations into three types and argues that appointing governors is a matter of ijtihad, so Uthman's actions are justified.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear or read criticism of a respected figure from Islamic history, like Uthman, do you immediately accept it or do you pause to consider whether it might be fabricated, a matter of ijtihad, or even a good deed? What does your reaction reveal about your trust in the justice of the Sahaba?
?
Have you ever judged someone's action without knowing the full context, only to later realize it was a matter of legitimate ijtihad or even a good deed? How can this lesson change your approach to evaluating others, especially those in authority?
?
The author argues that Uthman's piety and sincerity give us confidence in his decisions. If you were in a position where your decisions were criticized, could you be confident that your piety and sincerity would be recognized? What steps can you take to strengthen your sincerity (ikhlas) so that your actions are above reproach?

Defending Uthman's Appointments: The Case of Each Governor
The author provides individual defenses for four governors.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author defends each of Uthman's appointed relatives by showing their competence or prior appointment by Umar.

Core Idea
Each relative governor was competent or appointed by Umar, proving Uthman's ijtihad was sound.

This lesson continues the defense of Uthman by examining each of the named governors individually. The author shows that Muawiya, al-Walid, Sa'id, and Abd Allah ibn Amir were either appointed by Umar or proven capable through their actions. This refutes the claim of nepotism.

Guided Path
1
Read about Muawiya and al-Walid
The text shows both were appointed by Umar; Uthman only confirmed or continued them.
Muawiya over Syria, al-Walid over al-Jazira and Kufa.
2
Read about Sa'id ibn al-As
Sa'id was recognized by Umar as competent; no two differed on his ability.
He was also raised by Uthman but that doesn't affect his competence.
3
Read about Abd Allah ibn Amir
He was young but capable, conquered vast lands and ended the Sassanid empire.
His competence is proven by his achievements.
4
Draw the conclusion
All governors were either appointed by Umar or proven competent, refuting the nepotism claim.
Uthman's ijtihad was correct.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
رد ما ينسب إلى عثمان من الأحداث : يذكر المؤرخون أشياء كان الناقمون على عثمان قد اتخذوها أسباباً لثورتهم عليه، ومن هذه الأشياء ما هو مفترى على عثمان قطعاً، ومنها لو صح لم يكن موضع إنكار ، وإنما هو من قبيل ما يرجع إلى اجتهاد الإمام، ويقع مثله من الخلفاء الراشدين، ومنها ما يعد من حسناته وصالح أعماله. وها نحن هؤلاء نعرض على حضراتكم ما قصه المؤرخون وبعض المحدثين من الأمور التي طعن بها الطاعنون في عثمان، وجعلوها أسباب قيامهم عليه : قالوا: ولى عمالاً من ذوي قرابته، وزعموا أنهم ليسوا أهلاً للولاية، وذكروا معاوية بن أبي سفيان والوليد بن عقبة وعبد الله بن سعد بن أبي سرح، وسعيد بن العاص، وعبد الله بن عامر، ومروان بن الحكم. ويدفع هذا بأن تعيين الولاة يرجع إلى اجتهاد الإمام، وتقوى عثمان وإخلاصه في سياسة الرعية، يجعلنا على ثقة من أنه لو ولّى بعض ذوي قرابته بعد أن عرف كفايتهم للأعمال، والمعيب أن يولي قريباً لا يكون كافياً للعمل، أو يؤثره في الولاية وهو على علم بأن غيره أكفى منه، ثم إن معاوية ولاه الشام عمر بن الخطاب، ولم يزد عثمان على أن أقره على الولاية، وكذلك الوليد بـن عقبة كان عاملاً لعمر بن الخطاب على الجزيرة، وكان من عثمان أن ولاه الكوفة، فقدمها وسار في الناس خمس سنين سيرة حسنة، حتى اتهمه جماعة بشرب الخمر فاستقدمه عثمان وأقام عليه الحد، وولى مكانه سعيد بن العاص، وسعيد بن العاص نشأ يتيماً في حجر عثمان، ثم انتقل إلى الشام، وأقام بها عند معاوية، فذكره عمر بن الخطاب يوماً، واستقدمه إلى المدينة وأكرمه، وكان شريف النفس سخي اليد فصيح اللسان لا يختلف اثنان في كفايته للعمل الله وأما عبد بن عامر بن كريز، فكان ابن خال عثمان وأمه أم حكيم ابنة عبد المطلب، عمة النبي ، وعبد الله بن عامر هذا نشأ في الإسلام نشأة طيبة، وكان معدوداً من نجباء قريش وكرمائهم، ولاه عثمان عاملاً بالبصرة عند اختلاف أهلها على أبي موسى الأشعري، وكان سن عبد الله بن عامر يومئذ خمساً وعشرين سنة فقاد الجيوش، وفتح خراسان وسجستان وكرمان، ومازال يطارد كسرى يزدجرد حتى قتل كسرى وانقرضت على يده الدولة الساسانية، وكان لكرمه وحسن خلقه يحبه الناس.
Refutation of what is attributed to Uthman of events: The historians mention things that the critics of Uthman had taken as reasons for their revolt against him. Among these things are what is definitely fabricated against Uthman, and among them, even if true, would not be a matter of denial, but rather are of the type that go back to the ijtihad of the Imam, and similar occurs from the rightly guided caliphs, and among them are things that count among his good deeds and righteous works. Now we present to you what the historians and some hadith scholars have narrated of the matters by which the critics reviled Uthman and made them causes for their rising against him: They said: He appointed governors from among his relatives, and they claimed that they were not fit for governance, and they mentioned Muawiya ibn Abi Sufyan, al-Walid ibn Uqba, Abd Allah ibn Sa'd ibn Abi Sarh, Sa'id ibn al-As, Abd Allah ibn Amir, and Marwan ibn al-Hakam. This is rebutted by the fact that the appointment of governors goes back to the ijtihad of the Imam. The piety of Uthman and his sincerity in administering the subjects makes us confident that if he appointed some of his relatives, it was after he knew their competence for the work. The blameworthy is to appoint a relative who is not competent for the work, or to prefer him in governance while knowing that another is more competent than him. Moreover, Muawiya was appointed over Syria by Umar ibn al-Khattab, and Uthman only confirmed him in the governorship. Similarly, al-Walid ibn Uqba was a governor for Umar ibn al-Khattab over al-Jazira, and it was from Uthman that he appointed him over Kufa. He came to Kufa and conducted himself among the people for five years with good conduct, until a group accused him of drinking wine, so Uthman summoned him and carried out the prescribed punishment on him, and appointed Sa'id ibn al-As in his place. Sa'id ibn al-As grew up as an orphan in the care of Uthman, then moved to Syria and stayed there with Muawiya. Umar ibn al-Khattab mentioned him one day, summoned him to Medina, and honored him. He was noble in spirit, generous of hand, eloquent of tongue; no two persons differed about his competence for the work. As for Abd Allah ibn Amir ibn Kurayz, he was the maternal cousin of Uthman, his mother was Umm Hakim bint Abd al-Muttalib, the aunt of the Prophet. This Abd Allah ibn Amir grew up in Islam with a good upbringing, and was counted among the cleverest and most generous of Quraysh. Uthman appointed him as governor of Basra when its people differed over Abu Musa al-Ash'ari. At that time Abd Allah ibn Amir was twenty-five years old. He led armies, conquered Khurasan, Sijistan, and Kirman, and continued to pursue Chosroes Yazdegerd until he killed him and the Sassanid empire came to an end at his hands. Because of his generosity and good character, people loved him.
Source pages p. 174

Commentary
This passage is a refutation (radd) of the accusations leveled against Caliph Uthman, specifically the claim that he appointed his relatives to governorships while they were unqualified. The author begins by categorizing the criticisms: some are outright fabrications, some if true would not be blameworthy because they fall under the ijtihad (independent reasoning) of the Imam and similar actions occurred from the other rightly guided caliphs, and some are actually among Uthman's good deeds. The main accusation presented is that Uthman appointed governors from his relatives, naming Muawiya ibn Abi Sufyan, al-Walid ibn Uqba, Abd Allah ibn Sa'd ibn Abi Sarh, Sa'id ibn al-As, Abd Allah ibn Amir, and Marwan ibn al-Hakam. The author then provides a three-part rebuttal. First, he states a general principle: the appointment of governors is a matter of ijtihad, and Uthman's piety and sincerity give us confidence that he only appointed relatives after verifying their competence. The blameworthy act would be to appoint an incompetent relative, not to appoint a competent one. Second, he addresses each named governor individually: Muawiya was originally appointed by Umar, so Uthman merely confirmed him. Al-Walid ibn Uqba was also a governor under Umar; Uthman appointed him to Kufa, where he had a good record for five years, and when he was accused of drinking, Uthman applied the legal punishment and replaced him with Sa'id ibn al-As. Sa'id ibn al-As, though raised by Uthman, was recognized by Umar as competent and was honored by him. Abd Allah ibn Amir was also competent: he was of noble character, appointed at a young age, and he conquered vast territories and ended the Sassanid empire. Thus, each governor was either appointed by Umar or proven competent by their actions. The defense relies on historical precedent and the character of the individuals, concluding that the accusation of nepotism is unfounded.

The Attack on Uthman and the Role of Muhammad ibn Abi Bakr
A historical report defending Muhammad ibn Abi Bakr's honor.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the historical context of the attack on Caliph Uthman and the nuanced role of Muhammad ibn Abi Bakr, including why he was not considered a Companion and how the text defends his honor.

Core Idea
Muhammad ibn Abi Bakr's involvement is nuanced: he was not a Companion and he withdrew before the murder.

This passage from Imam al-Ash'ari's al-Ibanah addresses a sensitive historical event: the siege and killing of Caliph Uthman. It mentions Muhammad ibn Abi Bakr among those who entered his house, but immediately clarifies his status and provides a mitigating account. Let's examine how the text defends his honor and maintains respect for all involved.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the sequence: attack → mention of Muhammad → clarification → mitigating account.
2
Identify the key figures
Identify the rebels (الثائرين), Uthman, and Muhammad ibn Abi Bakr. Understand their roles as described.
The text explicitly states the rebels intended to kill Uthman.
3
Understand the clarification about Companionship
The text says Muhammad ibn Abi Bakr was not among the Companions because he was born in the year of the Farewell Pilgrimage, after which the Prophet died. This means he never met the Prophet as a believer.
This clarification exonerates him from the high rank of Companionship and implies his actions are not judged by that standard.
4
Examine the mitigating account
The text adds that some narrations say Muhammad ibn Abi Bakr entered, spoke to Uthman, admonished him, and then withdrew. The murder was committed by 'the foolish ones' afterwards.
This shows that he was not directly involved in the killing; he attempted to advise Uthman.
5
Reflect on the purpose
Consider why the author includes this detail. It defends the honor of Muhammad ibn Abi Bakr (son of Abu Bakr al-Siddiq) and provides a balanced historical account that avoids blaming a prominent figure.
This reflects the scholarly concern for justice and the good name of the Companions and their families.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم إن هؤلاء الثائرين اقتحموا دار عثمان يريدون قتله. ويذكر المؤرخون في أسماء من باشروا قتله محمد بن أبي بكر الصديق، ومحمد بن أبي بكر لم يكن من الصحابة لأنه ولد سنة حجة الوداع، وهي السنة التي انتقل عقبها النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم إلى الرفيق الأعلى، فكان أيام فتنة عثمان لم يزل في أوائل الشباب على أن بعض الروايات تقول: إن محمد بن أبي بكر بعد أن دخل على عثمان كلّمه ووعظه فرجع، ثم دخل سفهاء القوم، فسفكوا دمه الطاهر وكتاب الله بين يديه وصعدت روحه الطاهرة إلى مقام كريم.
Then these rebels stormed the house of Uthman intending to kill him. The historians mention among the names of those who directly participated in his killing Muhammad ibn Abi Bakr al-Siddiq. And Muhammad ibn Abi Bakr was not among the Companions because he was born in the year of the Farewell Pilgrimage, which is the year after which the Prophet, may God's peace and blessings be upon him, passed to the Highest Companion. So during the days of the Fitna of Uthman, he was still in early youth. However, some narrations say that Muhammad ibn Abi Bakr, after entering upon Uthman, spoke to him and admonished him, then he withdrew. Then the foolish ones of the people entered and shed his pure blood while the Book of God was before him, and his pure soul ascended to a noble station.
Source pages p. 174

Commentary
This passage reports the attack on Uthman's house. It clarifies that Muhammad ibn Abi Bakr, listed among the attackers, was not a Companion because he was born after the Prophet's death. It also mentions a mitigating account: Muhammad ibn Abi Bakr initially entered to admonish Uthman, then withdrew only to have others commit the murder. The passage thus defends Muhammad ibn Abi Bakr's honor by noting his late birth and his intention to advise rather than kill.

Key Terms
الثائرين
الصحابة
فتنة عثمان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That Muhammad ibn Abi Bakr was a Companion of the Prophet and directly involved in killing Uthman without any nuance.
Correction: The text clarifies he was not a Companion (born after Prophet's death) and that he withdrew after admonishing Uthman, so he did not participate in the murder.

Checkpoint
Why was Muhammad ibn Abi Bakr not considered a Companion of the Prophet?
A) He was killed before the Prophet's death.
B) He was born after the Prophet's death.
C) He apostatized after the Prophet's death.
D) He never met the Prophet.

Key Takeaway
This passage shows how early Muslim historians defended the honor of figures associated with the Fitna by providing contextual details and mitigating narratives.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear a negative report about someone from Islamic history, do you instinctively accept it or do you seek the full context? This passage shows how a simple clarification (age, status, sequence) can change the entire picture. What reputation have you unjustly held about a person from the past, and will you now re-examine it?
?
Muhammad ibn Abi Bakr was only a youth, not a Companion, yet his actions are still scrutinized. How does knowing someone's age and status affect the way you judge their deeds? Are you too quick to assign blame without considering their maturity or position? Make a commitment today to pause and ask: 'What do I not know about this person's circumstance?'
?
If you were in a situation where a close relative was falsely implicated in a great wrong, like the son of Abu Bakr here, would you have the courage to speak up and clarify the facts, even if it meant going against a popular narrative? This passage took a stand for truth. What false narrative about someone you know are you allowing to go unchallenged because it is easier to stay silent?

Defending Uthman's Appointments
Refutes accusation of nepotism against Uthman

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the principles by which the accusation that Uthman appointed unqualified relatives is refuted, including the concept of the imam's ijtihad and the specific qualifications of each appointee.

Core Idea
Uthman's appointments were based on ijtihad and competence, not nepotism.

This passage addresses one of the main accusations leveled against Uthman: that he appointed his relatives as governors. The author first categorizes the accusations, then provides a general principle of ijtihad, and finally defends each appointee individually, showing their qualifications and that some were actually appointed by Umar.

Guided Path
1
Categorize the accusations
Read the opening lines where the author divides the accusations into three types: fabrications, matters of ijtihad, and good deeds. Notice that the appointment of relatives is placed under matters of ijtihad.
This sets the framework for the refutation.
2
Understand the general refutation
The author states that appointing governors is a matter of ijtihad, and Uthman's piety ensures he would only appoint competent relatives. The blameworthy act is appointing an incompetent relative or favoring someone less qualified.
This is the key principle.
3
Examine each relative
Go through the list: Mu'awiya, al-Walid, Abdullah ibn Sa'd, Sa'id, Abdullah ibn Amir, Marwan. For each, note how the text shows they were either appointed by Umar or were clearly competent.
Pay attention to the specific defenses: Mu'awiya and al-Walid were already governors under Umar.
4
Reflect on the overall argument
Consider how this refutation defends Uthman's integrity. The passage not only answers the accusation but also highlights the achievements of the appointees, like Abdullah ibn Amir's conquests.
This shows the accusers were unjust.

Refutation of what is attributed to Uthman of events: The historians mention things that the critics of Uthman had taken as reasons for their revolt against him. Among these things are what are definitely fabricated against Uthman, and among them, if they were true, would not be a matter of objection, but rather are of the type that falls under the ijtihad of the Imam, and similar occurs from the Rightly Guided Caliphs, and among them are what are counted among his good deeds and righteous works. Here we present to you what the historians and some hadith scholars have narrated of the matters by which the critics have attacked Uthman, and made them reasons for rising against him: They said: He appointed governors from among his relatives, and they claimed that they were not qualified for governance, and they mentioned Mu'awiya ibn Abi Sufyan, al-Walid ibn Uqba, Abdullah ibn Sa'd ibn Abi Sarh, Sa'id ibn al-Aas, Abdullah ibn Amir, and Marwan ibn al-Hakam. This is refuted by the fact that the appointment of governors goes back to the ijtihad of the Imam, and the piety of Uthman and his sincerity in administering the subjects make us confident that if he appointed some of his relatives after knowing their sufficiency for the tasks. The blameworthy thing is to appoint a relative who is not sufficient for the work, or to favor him in governorship while knowing that someone else is more competent than him. Moreover, Mu'awiya was appointed over Sham by Umar ibn al-Khattab, and Uthman only confirmed him in the governorship. Similarly, al-Walid ibn Uqba was a governor for Umar ibn al-Khattab over al-Jazira, and from Uthman was that he appointed him over Kufa. He came to it and conducted himself among the people for five years with good conduct until a group accused him of drinking wine, so Uthman summoned him and applied the prescribed punishment against him, and appointed in his place Sa'id ibn al-Aas. Sa'id ibn al-Aas grew up an orphan under the care of Uthman, then moved to Sham and lived there with Mu'awiya. Umar ibn al-Khattab mentioned him one day, summoned him to Medina and honored him. He was noble of spirit, generous of hand, eloquent of tongue; no two people differed on his sufficiency for the work. As for Abdullah ibn Amir ibn Kurayz, he was the maternal cousin of Uthman, and his mother was Umm Hakim bint Abd al-Muttalib, the aunt of the Prophet. This Abdullah ibn Amir grew up in Islam with a good upbringing, and was counted among the nobles and generous ones of Quraysh. Uthman appointed him as governor over Basra when its people differed with Abu Musa al-Ash'ari. The age of Abdullah ibn Amir that day was twenty-five years. He led armies, conquered Khurasan, Sijistan, and Kirman, and continued to pursue Chosroes Yazdegerd until Chosroes was killed and the Sassanid state was extinguished at his hands. And because of his generosity and good character, the people loved him.
Source pages p. 174

Commentary
This passage begins the refutation of accusations against Uthman. It first categorizes the accusations: some are false, some are matters of ijtihad, some are actually good deeds. Then it lists the specific accusation of appointing relatives: Mu'awiya, al-Walid, etc. The refutation has two parts: (1) a general principle that appointment is by ijtihad, and Uthman's piety ensures he would only appoint competent relatives; favoritism is blameworthy only if the relative is incompetent. (2) For each named appointee, the text shows they were either already appointed by Umar (Mu'awiya, al-Walid) or were known for competence (Sa'id, Abdullah ibn Amir). It highlights Abdullah ibn Amir's achievements: young age but successful conquests. The tone is defensive, arguing that Uthman acted correctly.

Key Terms
اجتهاد الإمام
ولاة
الخلفاء الراشدين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That Uthman arbitrarily appointed his relatives without considering their qualifications.
Correction: The passage shows that Uthman acted based on ijtihad and only appointed relatives after confirming their competence, and many were previously appointed by Umar.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the general principle that justifies Uthman appointing his relatives?
A) It was his right as caliph to appoint anyone.
B) Appointing governors falls under the ijtihad of the Imam, and he would only appoint those he knew were competent.
C) He was forced to appoint them due to tribal pressure.
D) He did it to remove them from Medina.

Key Takeaway
The accusation of nepotism against Uthman is refuted by showing that his appointments were based on competence and ijtihad, and many appointees were previously chosen by Umar.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear criticism of a leader, do you assume the worst or give them the benefit of the doubt, as this lesson urges regarding Uthman? What steps can you take to seek balanced information before forming an opinion?
?
This lesson shows that Uthman's decisions were based on ijtihad and competence. In your own life, when you make decisions that affect others, do you investigate thoroughly or rely on assumptions? How can you apply the principle of ijtihad to your own choices?
?
The critics of Uthman mistook his actions for nepotism. Have you ever misjudged someone's motives only to later discover they had valid reasons? How can this lesson cultivate humility in your judgments of others, especially those in authority?

The Defense of Abdullah ibn Sa'd
Defends Uthman's appointment of Abdullah ibn Sa'd and responds to apostasy accusation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Uthman's appointment of Abdullah ibn Sa'd is defended, including the response to his apostasy and the evidence from the conquest of Africa.

Core Idea
Repentance wipes out past sins, and Abdullah ibn Sa'd's later deeds proved his sincerity.

This lesson focuses on the first major accusation against Uthman: his appointment of Abdullah ibn Sa'd, who had apostatized before. The passage explains the circumstances of the appointment and rebuts the charge with arguments from history and Islamic principle.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage about Abdullah ibn Sa'd
Carefully read the Arabic text and translation covering Uthman's appointment and the defense.
Note the mention of the conquest of Africa and the Companions who participated.
2
Understand the apostasy rebuttal
The passage responds to the accusation of apostasy by stating that he returned to Islam and repentance wipes out the past.
This is a key theological principle: repentance erases previous sins.
3
Analyze the evidence of approval
The conquest of Africa with many Companions and their sons is presented as a sign that the Companions approved of his leadership.
This is a practical argument from consensus.
4
Reflect on the overall defense
Consider how Uthman's decision is justified through both textual and historical evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما عبد الله سعد بن بن أبي سرح فكان عثمان استعمله على الحرب في مصر، وأبقى عمرو ابن العاص على الخراج ثم وقع خلاف بينهما، فاستقدم عثمان عمرو بن العاص، وصارت إمارتا الخراج والحرب إلى عبد الله سعد بن وذكر ابن عبد البر في كتاب ( الاستيعاب ) سبباً آخر لعزل عمرو بن العاص، هو أن الاسكندرية انتقضت سنة (٢٥هـ) فافتتحها عمرو بن العاص، وعاملهم معاملة الناقضين للعهد، ولم يصح عند عثمان نقضهم، فعزله وولى عبد الله بن سرح فاعتزل عمرو إلى ناحية بفلسطين، وكان يزور المدينة أحياناً . ويدلكم على أن ولاية عبد الله بن سعد لم تقع موقع الإنكار من الصحابة، أن عثمان أمره بفتح أفريقية، فسار إليها في جيش مؤلف من كثير من الصحابة وأبناء الصحابة منهم : عبد الله بن عمر، وعبد الرحمن ابن أبي بكر، وعبد الله بن الزبير، وعبد الله بن جعفر، والحسن والحسين، بن عمرو بن العاص وعبد الله وقالوا: عبد الله بن سعد هذا كان أسلم ثم ارتد، وعاد إلى مكة، فنقول: عاد إلى الإسلام، وظهر إخلاصه والتوبة تجب ما قبلها، قال أبو بكر بن العربي في ( كتاب العارضة ) : ولّى بن سعد بن أبي سرح لحسن سيرته وحميد طريقته، ولهذا فتح الفتوح في بحر عثمان عبد الله المغرب وبره وغزا معه جماعة من الصحابة وأبناء الصحابة، أطاعوه ورضوا عنه. وأما مروان بن الحكم فكان له عندما توفي رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ثمان سنين، وتولى الكتابة لعثمان، وروى الحديث عن عثمان وعلي والواقع أن مروان قد كثر الطعن فيه، ونرى بعض المحدثين يصفه بما يخفف هذا الطعن فأبو بكر بن العربي يقول : ( فمروان رجل عدل، من كبار الأمة عند الصحابة والتابعين وفقهاء المسلمين ) . وقالوا رد الحكم إلى المدينة وقد نفاه النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم منها إلى الطائف ويدفع هذا بأن النبي قد أذن قبل وفاته لعثمان في رده، ولما أبلغ عثمان هذا الإذن أبا بكر وعمر، قالا له: إن كان معك شهيد رددناه ولما ولي عثمان الخلافة عمل على مقتضى علمه بأن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قد أذن في رده، وللحاكم أن يعمل على ما يعلم في غير القضاء بين الخصوم. وقالوا: كان عمر يضرب بالدرة وهو يضرب بالسوط وضرب عمار بن ياسر وابن مسعود ومنعه عطاءه، وضرب أبا ذر ونفاه إلى الربذة. وسلك بعض أهل العلم في دفع هذا الإنكار طريقة أن للحاكم أن يؤدب بعض الرعايا بمـا يـراه صلاحاً، ولكن حفاظ الحديث أنكروا هذا الذي يحكيه المؤرخون أشد الإنكار، قال أبو بكر بن العربي في ( كتاب العواصم : أما ضربه لعمار وابن مسعود ومنعه لعطاء ابن مسعوده فزور وإفك، وقد اعتذر عن ذلك العلماء بوجوه لا ينبغي أن يُشتغل بها، لأنها مبنية على باطل، ولا يبنى حق على باطل، ولا يذهب الزمان في مماشاة الجهال، فإن ذلك لا آخر له.
As for Abdullah Sa'd ibn ibn Abi Sarh, Uthman appointed him over war in Egypt, and kept Amr ibn al-Aas over the land tax. Then a dispute occurred between them, so Uthman summoned Amr ibn al-Aas, and both the emirates of land tax and war went to Abdullah Sa'd ibn. Ibn Abd al-Barr mentioned in the book al-Isti'ab another reason for the dismissal of Amr ibn al-Aas: that Alexandria broke the treaty in the year 25 AH, so Amr ibn al-Aas conquered it and treated them as treaty-breakers, but Uthman did not confirm their breach, so he dismissed him and appointed Abdullah ibn Sarh. Amr then withdrew to a region in Palestine, and he used to visit Medina occasionally. And this indicates that the governorship of Abdullah ibn Sa'd did not fall into the place of disapproval among the Companions: Uthman ordered him to conquer Africa, so he marched to it with an army composed of many Companions and sons of Companions, among them: Abdullah ibn Umar, Abd al-Rahman ibn Abi Bakr, Abdullah ibn al-Zubayr, Abdullah ibn Ja'far, al-Hasan and al-Husayn, bin Amr ibn al-Aas and Abdullah. And they said: This Abdullah ibn Sa'd had accepted Islam then apostatized and returned to Mecca. So we say: He returned to Islam, and his sincerity became apparent, and repentance wipes out what came before it. Abu Bakr ibn al-Arabi said in Kitab al-Arida: He appointed ibn Sa'd ibn Abi Sarh because of his good conduct and praiseworthy method, and for this reason he achieved the conquests in the sea of Uthman Abdullah the Maghreb and its land, and a group of Companions and sons of Companions raided with him, obeying him and being pleased with him. As for Marwan ibn al-Hakam, he was eight years old when the Messenger of God died, and he became the secretary for Uthman, and narrated hadith from Uthman and Ali. The reality is that Marwan has been heavily criticized, and we see some hadith scholars describing him in a way that mitigates this criticism. Abu Bakr ibn al-Arabi says: 'Marwan is a just man, from the greats of the Ummah according to the Companions, Successors, and jurists of the Muslims.' And they said: He returned al-Hakam to Medina while the Prophet had exiled him from it to Ta'if. This is refuted by the fact that the Prophet before his death permitted Uthman to return him. When Uthman informed Abu Bakr and Umar of this permission, they said to him: 'If you have a witness, we would return him.' When Uthman became caliph, he acted according to his knowledge that the Messenger of God had permitted his return, and the ruler may act on what he knows outside of adjudication between adversaries. And they said: Umar used to strike with the darra, while he strikes with the whip, and he struck Ammar ibn Yasir and Ibn Mas'ud and withheld his stipend, and he struck Abu Dhar and exiled him to al-Rabdha. Some scholars have taken the approach in refuting this denial that the ruler may discipline some of the subjects as he sees fit as a matter of reform. However, the hadith preservers have most severely denied what the historians narrate. Abu Bakr ibn al-Arabi said in Kitab al-Awasim: 'As for his striking Ammar and Ibn Mas'ud and withholding Ibn Mas'ud's stipend, that is falsehood and slander. Scholars have excused that with explanations that should not be occupied with, because they are based on falsehood. Truth is not built on falsehood, and time should not be spent in keeping company with the ignorant, for that has no end.'
Source pages p. 174

Commentary
This passage continues the defense of Uthman's appointments and addresses further accusations. It defends Abdullah ibn Sa'd by noting that Uthman appointed him after dismissing Amr ibn al-Aas due to the latter's harsh treatment of Alexandria. It shows that many Companions and their sons accompanied Abdullah ibn Sa'd in the conquest of Africa, indicating their approval. Regarding Abdullah ibn Sa'd's apostasy, the passage says he returned to Islam and repentance wipes out past sins. It also defends Marwan ibn al-Hakam by citing Abu Bakr ibn al-Arabi who calls him just and from the greats. The accusation of returning al-Hakam (Marwan's father) to Medina is refuted by stating that the Prophet permitted it, and Uthman acted on that knowledge. Finally, the accusation of Uthman using a whip and beating Ammar, Ibn Mas'ud, and Abu Dhar is addressed: some scholars say a ruler may discipline as needed, but hadith scholars deny the reports as slander. The passage ends with a quote from Abu Bakr ibn al-Arabi rejecting those accusations as false and not worth engaging.

Key Terms
الردة
التوبة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That Abdullah ibn Sa'd remained an apostate and should not have been trusted.
Correction: The passage argues he repented sincerely, and his later actions (conquests with many Companions) prove his good standing.

Checkpoint
What evidence does the passage use to show that the Companions approved of Abdullah ibn Sa'd's governorship?
A) He was appointed by the Prophet.
B) Many Companions and their sons joined him in the conquest of Africa.
C) He was known for his piety.
D) Umar praised him publicly.

Key Takeaway
Uthman's appointment of Abdullah ibn Sa'd is defended by his repentance, good conduct, and the approval of many Companions who fought under him.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever judged someone based on their past sins, forgetting that repentance can transform them completely? Will you actively seek to see people's present deeds rather than their past mistakes?
?
This passage shows that the Companions trusted Abdullah ibn Sa'd after his repentance. Is there someone in your life whom you have refused to trust because of a past wrongdoing? What concrete step will you take this week to extend that trust?
?
The lesson emphasizes that repentance wipes out what came before. Is there a sin from your past that you still carry guilt over, despite having repented? How will you internalize the truth that Allah's forgiveness is complete and final, freeing you to move forward without burden?

The Defense of Marwan ibn al-Hakam
Defends Marwan ibn al-Hakam and addresses the return of his father al-Hakam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the passage defends Marwan ibn al-Hakam against criticism, including his character and the issue of his father's return to Medina.

Core Idea
Marwan was a just figure among the greats of the Ummah, and his father's return was permitted by the Prophet.

This lesson addresses the second major defense: that of Marwan ibn al-Hakam, a close aide of Uthman. The passage counters accusations about his background, his narration of hadith, and the controversial return of his father al-Hakam from exile.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on Marwan
Read the Arabic and translation covering the defense of Marwan.
Note the reference to his age at the Prophet's death and his role as secretary.
2
Understand the character defense
Abu Bakr ibn al-Arabi is quoted praising Marwan as just and from the greats of the Ummah.
This is an authoritative opinion from a respected scholar.
3
Analyze the rebuttal regarding al-Hakam's return
The accusation that Uthman returned al-Hakam (Marwan's father) against the Prophet's exile is refuted by stating that the Prophet permitted it before his death, and Uthman acted on that knowledge.
The passage notes that Abu Bakr and Umar said they would have returned him with a witness.
4
Reflect on the ruler's discretion
The passage argues that a ruler can act on his knowledge outside of formal adjudication.

This passage continues the defense of Uthman's appointments and addresses further accusations. It defends Abdullah ibn Sa'd by noting that Uthman appointed him after dismissing Amr ibn al-Aas due to the latter's harsh treatment of Alexandria. It shows that many Companions and their sons accompanied Abdullah ibn Sa'd in the conquest of Africa, indicating their approval. Regarding Abdullah ibn Sa'd's apostasy, the passage says he returned to Islam and repentance wipes out past sins. It also defends Marwan ibn al-Hakam by citing Abu Bakr ibn al-Arabi who calls him just and from the greats. The accusation of returning al-Hakam (Marwan's father) to Medina is refuted by stating that the Prophet permitted it, and Uthman acted on that knowledge. Finally, the accusation of Uthman using a whip and beating Ammar, Ibn Mas'ud, and Abu Dhar is addressed: some scholars say a ruler may discipline as needed, but hadith scholars deny the reports as slander. The passage ends with a quote from Abu Bakr ibn al-Arabi rejecting those accusations as false and not worth engaging.

Key Terms
الحكم بن أبي العاص

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That Uthman returned al-Hakam against the explicit command of the Prophet.
Correction: The text states the Prophet permitted the return before his death, and Uthman had knowledge of this.

Checkpoint
What was Abu Bakr and Umar's response when Uthman told them about the Prophet's permission to return al-Hakam?
A) They immediately agreed.
B) They said they would need a witness.
C) They refused outright.
D) They asked Uthman to exile him again.

Key Takeaway
Marwan is defended as a just figure, and the return of his father al-Hakam is justified by the Prophet's prior permission.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever held a negative opinion about someone based on incomplete information? What would it take for you to change that opinion in light of new evidence, as the author presents here for Marwan?
?
The Prophet gave permission for al-Hakam's return before his death. Is there someone you have permanently 'banished' from your life that you should reconsider? What is preventing you from allowing them back?
?
Uthman acted on his knowledge even without a formal witness. Are there truths you know but are afraid to act on because others might not accept them? How can you develop the courage to follow your conviction?

Rejection of Accusations against Uthman's Discipline
Responds to accusations of Uthman beating Companions and using a whip.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the passage responds to accusations that Uthman used a whip and beat Companions, and why some scholars dismiss these reports as slander.

Core Idea
Accusations that Uthman beat Ammar, Ibn Mas'ud, and Abu Dhar are rejected as false and based on unreliable reports.

This final lesson from the passage addresses serious accusations about Uthman's use of force against prominent Companions. The author presents a range of responses, including outright denial by hadith scholars and a principle that rulers may discipline, but ultimately dismisses the reports as slander.

Guided Path
1
Read the accusation and responses
Read the Arabic text detailing the accusations and the different scholarly responses.
Note the contrast between some scholars' justification and the hadith scholars' denial.
2
Understand the justification approach
Some scholars argued that a ruler may discipline subjects as needed.
This is a general legal principle.
3
Analyze the hadith scholars' denial
They reject the reports as slander. Abu Bakr ibn al-Arabi calls them false and not worth engaging.
This is a strong rejection.
4
Reflect on the overall approach
Consider how the passage uses both justification and denial to defend Uthman.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما عبد الله سعد بن بن أبي سرح فكان عثمان استعمله على الحرب في مصر، وأبقى عمرو ابن العاص على الخراج ثم وقع خلاف بينهما، فاستقدم عثمان عمرو بن العاص، وصارت إمارتا الخراج والحرب إلى عبد الله سعد بن وذكر ابن عبد البر في كتاب ( الاستيعاب ) سبباً آخر لعزل عمرو بن العاص، هو أن الاسكندرية انتقضت سنة (٢٥هـ) فافتتحها عمرو بن العاص، وعاملهم معاملة الناقضين للعهد، ولم يصح عند عثمان نقضهم، فعزله وولى عبد الله بن سرح فاعتزل عمرو إلى ناحية بفلسطين، وكان يزور المدينة أحياناً . ويدلكم على أن ولاية عبد الله بن سعد لم تقع موقع الإنكار من الصحابة، أن عثمان أمره بفتح أفريقية، فسار إليها في جيش مؤلف من كثير من الصحابة وأبناء الصحابة منهم : عبد الله بن عمر، وعبد الرحمن ابن أبي بكر، وعبد الله بن الزبير، وعبد الله بن جعفر، والحسن والحسين، بن عمرو بن العاص وعبد الله وقالوا: عبد الله بن سعد هذا كان أسلم ثم ارتد، وعاد إلى مكة، فنقول: عاد إلى الإسلام، وظهر إخلاصه والتوبة تجب ما قبلها، قال أبو بكر بن العربي في ( كتاب العارضة ) : ولّى بن سعد بن أبي سرح لحسن سيرته وحميد طريقته، ولهذا فتح الفتوح في بحر عثمان عبد الله المغرب وبره وغزا معه جماعة من الصحابة وأبناء الصحابة، أطاعوه ورضوا عنه. وأما مروان بن الحكم فكان له عندما توفي رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ثمان سنين، وتولى الكتابة لعثمان، وروى الحديث عن عثمان وعلي والواقع أن مروان قد كثر الطعن فيه، ونرى بعض المحدثين يصفه بما يخفف هذا الطعن فأبو بكر بن العربي يقول : ( فمروان رجل عدل، من كبار الأمة عند الصحابة والتابعين وفقهاء المسلمين ) . وقالوا رد الحكم إلى المدينة وقد نفاه النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم منها إلى الطائف ويدفع هذا بأن النبي قد أذن قبل وفاته لعثمان في رده، ولما أبلغ عثمان هذا الإذن أبا بكر وعمر، قالا له: إن كان معك شهيد رددناه ولما ولي عثمان الخلافة عمل على مقتضى علمه بأن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قد أذن في رده، وللحاكم أن يعمل على ما يعلم في غير القضاء بين الخصوم. وقالوا: كان عمر يضرب بالدرة وهو يضرب بالسوط وضرب عمار بن ياسر وابن مسعود ومنعه عطاءه، وضرب أبا ذر ونفاه إلى الربذة. وسلك بعض أهل العلم في دفع هذا الإنكار طريقة أن للحاكم أن يؤدب بعض الرعايا بمـا يـراه صلاحاً، ولكن حفاظ الحديث أنكروا هذا الذي يحكيه المؤرخون أشد الإنكار، قال أبو بكر بن العربي في ( كتاب العواصم : أما ضربه لعمار وابن مسعود ومنعه لعطاء ابن مسعوده فزور وإفك، وقد اعتذر عن ذلك العلماء بوجوه لا ينبغي أن يُشتغل بها، لأنها مبنية على باطل، ولا يبنى حق على باطل، ولا يذهب الزمان في مماشاة الجهال، فإن ذلك لا آخر له.
As for Abdullah Sa'd ibn ibn Abi Sarh, Uthman appointed him over war in Egypt, and kept Amr ibn al-Aas over the land tax. Then a dispute occurred between them, so Uthman summoned Amr ibn al-Aas, and both the emirates of land tax and war went to Abdullah Sa'd ibn. Ibn Abd al-Barr mentioned in the book al-Isti'ab another reason for the dismissal of Amr ibn al-Aas: that Alexandria broke the treaty in the year 25 AH, so Amr ibn al-Aas conquered it and treated them as treaty-breakers, but Uthman did not confirm their breach, so he dismissed him and appointed Abdullah ibn Sarh. Amr then withdrew to a region in Palestine, and he used to visit Medina occasionally. And this indicates that the governorship of Abdullah ibn Sa'd did not fall into the place of disapproval among the Companions: Uthman ordered him to conquer Africa, so he marched to it with an army composed of many Companions and sons of Companions, among them: Abdullah ibn Umar, Abd al-Rahman ibn Abi Bakr, Abdullah ibn al-Zubayr, Abdullah ibn Ja'far, al-Hasan and al-Husayn, bin Amr ibn al-Aas and Abdullah. And they said: This Abdullah ibn Sa'd had accepted Islam then apostatized and returned to Mecca. So we say: He returned to Islam, and his sincerity became apparent, and repentance wipes out what came before it. Abu Bakr ibn al-Arabi said in Kitab al-Arida: He appointed ibn Sa'd ibn Abi Sarh because of his good conduct and praiseworthy method, and for this reason he achieved the conquests in the sea of Uthman Abdullah the Maghreb and its land, and a group of Companions and sons of Companions raided with him, obeying him and being pleased with him. As for Marwan ibn al-Hakam, he was eight years old when the Messenger of God died, and he became the secretary for Uthman, and narrated hadith from Uthman and Ali. The reality is that Marwan has been heavily criticized, and we see some hadith scholars describing him in a way that mitigates this criticism. Abu Bakr ibn al-Arabi says: 'Marwan is a just man, from the greats of the Ummah according to the Companions, Successors, and jurists of the Muslims.' And they said: He returned al-Hakam to Medina while the Prophet had exiled him from it to Ta'if. This is refuted by the fact that the Prophet before his death permitted Uthman to return him. When Uthman informed Abu Bakr and Umar of this permission, they said to him: 'If you have a witness, we would return him.' When Uthman became caliph, he acted according to his knowledge that the Messenger of God had permitted his return, and the ruler may act on what he knows outside of adjudication between adversaries. And they said: Umar used to strike with the darra, while he strikes with the whip, and he struck Ammar ibn Yasir and Ibn Mas'ud and withheld his stipend, and he struck Abu Dhar and exiled him to al-Rabdha. Some scholars have taken the approach in refuting this denial that the ruler may discipline some of the subjects as he sees fit as a matter of reform. However, the hadith preservers have most severely denied what the historians narrate. Abu Bakr ibn al-Arabi said in Kitab al-Awasim: 'As for his striking Ammar and Ibn Mas'ud and withholding Ibn Mas'ud's stipend, that is falsehood and slander. Scholars have excused that with explanations that should not be occupied with, because they are based on falsehood. Truth is not built on falsehood, and time should not be spent in keeping company with the ignorant, for that has no end.'
Source pages p. 174

Commentary
This passage continues the defense of Uthman's appointments and addresses further accusations. It defends Abdullah ibn Sa'd by noting that Uthman appointed him after dismissing Amr ibn al-Aas due to the latter's harsh treatment of Alexandria. It shows that many Companions and their sons accompanied Abdullah ibn Sa'd in the conquest of Africa, indicating their approval. Regarding Abdullah ibn Sa'd's apostasy, the passage says he returned to Islam and repentance wipes out past sins. It also defends Marwan ibn al-Hakam by citing Abu Bakr ibn al-Arabi who calls him just and from the greats. The accusation of returning al-Hakam (Marwan's father) to Medina is refuted by stating that the Prophet permitted it, and Uthman acted on that knowledge. Finally, the accusation of Uthman using a whip and beating Ammar, Ibn Mas'ud, and Abu Dhar is addressed: some scholars say a ruler may discipline as needed, but hadith scholars deny the reports as slander. The passage ends with a quote from Abu Bakr ibn al-Arabi rejecting those accusations as false and not worth engaging.

الدرة
السوط

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That Uthman unjustly beat Companions is established historical fact.
Correction: The passage shows that hadith scholars consider these reports false and slanderous.

Checkpoint
How did the hadith preservers view the reports of Uthman beating Ammar and Ibn Mas'ud?
A) They considered them reliable.
B) They weakly accepted them.
C) They severely denied them as false.
